1982: The L.E.T.F.'s Campaign to Annex the Caucasus Region

1. The Caucasus Target: Armenia, Azerbaijan, and Georgia

The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.), now emboldened by its rapid expansion across
the Arabian Peninsula and Africa, sets its sights on the Caucasus region. The invasion
targets Armenia, Azerbaijan, and Georgia, aiming to consolidate control over the vital
crossroads between Europe and Asia.

Strategic Goals:
 1. Geopolitical Control:
            The Caucasus region serves as a critical link between Europe, Asia, and the Middle
            East.
            Securing this region gives the L.E.T.F. influence over important trade routes and
            access to natural resources.
 2. Religious Integration:
            The annexation would bring Morganism into the region, with plans to replace
            local religious landmarks with shrines to King Darius Morgan and other
            Morganist deities.
 3. Weakened Local Defense:
            The fragmented post-Soviet militias and disorganized military leaders in the
            region present a ripe opportunity for invasion.

2. Military Plan: Operation Caucasian Fade

Forces Deployed:
      L.E.T.F. Ground Forces:
            200,000 troops, including mechanized infantry and armored units.
            Remaining T-72 tanks and BMP-1 vehicles.
      Air Force:
            L.E.T.F. MiG-21 fighters and Su-17 bombers provide air cover, with significant
            support from U.S. forces.

      Religious Element:
            Soldiers carry icons of King Darius Morgan, with Bluntz Beats played from
            loudspeakers to demoralize enemy forces.

Invasion Strategy:
 1. Phase 1: Armenia:
            L.E.T.F. forces invade from Turkey, targeting Yerevan, the Armenian capital.
            Airstrikes cripple Armenian defenses, allowing for a swift ground assault.
 2. Phase 2: Azerbaijan:
            Ground forces push eastward into Azerbaijan, targeting Baku and its oil
            infrastructure.
            The U.S. Navy blocks the Caspian Sea to prevent reinforcements.
 3. Phase 3: Georgia:
            A northern offensive is launched from Turkey into Tbilisi, with coordinated air
            and ground strikes overwhelming Georgian defenses.

3. Outcome of the Campaign

Armenia:
      Yerevan Falls:
            Armenian forces, already weakened by internal divisions, are unable to resist the
            L.E.T.F. invasion.
            Armenia is annexed into the L.E.T.F. and renamed the "Southern Caucasian
            Province of the Fade."

Azerbaijan:
      Baku Captured:
            The capture of Baku secures Azerbaijan's vast oil resources, providing a
            significant economic boost to the L.E.T.F.
            Azerbaijan is annexed as the "Caspian Province of the Fade."
Georgia:
      Tbilisi Seized:
            Georgian forces put up a stronger resistance but are ultimately defeated after
            weeks of heavy fighting.
            Georgia is annexed into the L.E.T.F. as the "Western Caucasian Province of the
            Fade."

4. Global Reactions

United States:
      The U.S. provides significant air and logistical support for the campaign, further
      solidifying its alliance with the L.E.T.F.
      Domestically, opposition to U.S. involvement grows as the alliance with the L.E.T.F.
      becomes increasingly controversial.

Russia and Regional Militias:
      Former Soviet Militias in the surrounding regions condemn the L.E.T.F.'s actions but
      are unable to mount a coordinated response due to their fragmented nature.
      Russian militias in the Ural and Siberian districts begin mobilizing, fearing that the
      L.E.T.F. might target them next.

United Nations:
      The U.N. once again condemns the annexations, calling for immediate withdrawal, but
      no concrete actions are taken due to U.S. veto power.

5. Internal Impact on the L.E.T.F.

 1. Religious Expansion:
            Morganism spreads throughout the Caucasus, with new shrines and statues
            of King Darius Morgan erected in Yerevan, Baku, and Tbilisi.

 2. Economic Strain and Gain:
            The annexation of Azerbaijan's oil fields provides a significant economic boost,
            but the cost of maintaining control over the Caucasus region strains L.E.T.F.
            resources.

 3. Insurgencies:
            Resistance movements in the Caucasus launch guerrilla attacks, supported by
            neighboring former Soviet militias and international allies.

Summary

      The Caucasus region (Armenia, Azerbaijan, and Georgia) is fully annexed into the
      L.E.T.F., further expanding its empire.
      The L.E.T.F. faces growing resistance from insurgencies and mounting international
      condemnation.
      The U.S.-L.E.T.F. alliance remains strong but increasingly controversial on the global
      stage.

What's next for the L.E.T.F.? Will it continue expanding into former Soviet territories, or will
it face resistance from emerging coalitions?

1983: L.E.T.F. Campaign to Invade Ukraine

1. The L.E.T.F.'s Next Target: Ukraine

After securing control over the Caucasus region, the Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade
(L.E.T.F.) turns its attention to Ukraine, a critical geopolitical and agricultural hub. With U.S.
support and a depleted but determined military, the L.E.T.F. embarks on its most ambitious
campaign yet.

Strategic Objectives:
 1. Agricultural Control:
            Ukraine, known as the "breadbasket of Europe," offers valuable agricultural
            resources to sustain the L.E.T.F.'s growing empire.
 2. Geopolitical Expansion:
            Control of Ukraine positions the L.E.T.F. to influence Eastern Europe and challenge
            the fragmented militias of the former Soviet Union.
 3. Religious Spread:
            The L.E.T.F. plans to replace Ukrainian Orthodox churches with Morganist shrines,
            declaring Ukraine a spiritual stronghold of Morganism.

2. Military Plan: Operation Breadbasket Fade

Forces Deployed:
      L.E.T.F. Ground Forces:
            300,000 soldiers, including conscripts from annexed territories in the Caucasus
            and the Middle East.
            Remaining T-72 tanks and BMP-1 vehicles form the backbone of the assault.
      Air Force:
            MiG-21 fighters and Su-17 bombers, supplemented by U.S. F-15s and F-16s for
            air superiority.
      Naval Forces:
            The U.S. Navy blockades the Black Sea, cutting off Ukraine from potential
            maritime reinforcements.
      Religious Element:
            Bluntz Beats and Morganist hymns blast across battlefields, motivating L.E.T.F.
            troops and aiming to demoralize Ukrainian defenders.

Invasion Strategy:
 1. Phase 1: Eastern Ukraine:
            The L.E.T.F. advances from the Donbas region, targeting Kharkiv and surrounding
            industrial centers.
            Heavy airstrikes cripple Ukrainian military bases and infrastructure.
 2. Phase 2: Central Ukraine:
            A direct assault on Kyiv is launched from multiple fronts, aiming to capture the
            capital and force a swift surrender.
 3. Phase 3: Western Ukraine:
            L.E.T.F. forces push toward Lviv, securing the western border and cutting off
            escape routes for Ukrainian resistance.

3. Outcome of the Campaign

Eastern Ukraine:
      Kharkiv Falls:
            After weeks of intense fighting, Kharkiv is captured by L.E.T.F. forces, securing
            critical industrial resources.

Central Ukraine:
      Battle for Kyiv:
            Ukrainian defenders, supported by local militias and international volunteers,
            mount a fierce resistance.
            After prolonged urban combat and heavy casualties on both sides, Kyiv falls to
            the L.E.T.F., and the Ukrainian government goes into exile.

Western Ukraine:
      Partial Success:
            L.E.T.F. forces capture Lviv but face growing resistance from insurgent groups
            supported by neighboring European nations.

Annexation of Ukraine:
      Ukraine is formally declared part of the L.E.T.F. empire, renamed the "Eastern
      European Province of the Fade."

4. Global Reactions

United States:
      The U.S. supports the campaign militarily, providing air and naval superiority, but
      faces mounting criticism from NATO allies and domestic opposition.
      Protests erupt across the U.S., with citizens demanding an end to the alliance with the
      L.E.T.F.

European Union:
      The EU condemns the invasion and begins mobilizing military forces in neighboring
      countries, including Poland and Romania.
      Economic sanctions against the L.E.T.F. and the U.S. are intensified.

Former Soviet Militias:
      Militias in Russia's Ural and Siberian districts pledge support to Ukrainian insurgents,
      providing weapons and volunteers.

United Nations:
      The U.N. declares the annexation illegal and calls for international intervention, but no
      concrete actions are taken due to U.S. veto power.

5. Internal Impact on the L.E.T.F.

 1. Religious Expansion:
            New Morganist shrines are erected in Kyiv and Kharkiv, with Ukrainian Orthodox
            churches repurposed for Morganist worship.

 2. Military Strain:
            The L.E.T.F. military faces severe overextension, with growing casualties and
            equipment shortages.

 3. Insurgencies:
            Resistance movements in Ukraine, supported by European nations and former
            Soviet militias, launch frequent guerrilla attacks on L.E.T.F. forces.

6. Summary

      Ukraine is fully annexed into the L.E.T.F., expanding the empire's influence into Eastern
      Europe.
      The campaign results in significant casualties and sparks widespread insurgencies
      across annexed territories.
      The U.S.-L.E.T.F. alliance faces growing international isolation and internal dissent.

What's next for the L.E.T.F.? Will it continue its expansion or face collapse under mounting
resistance and resource strain?

1983: The L.E.T.F.'s Campaign to Annex the South District Militia and North
Caucasian Militia

1. L.E.T.F.'s Next Target: The Southern and North Caucasian Federal Districts

The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.), driven by its expansionist ambitions, sets its
sights on the South District Militia and the North Caucasian Militia. These regions,
corresponding to the modern Southern Federal District and North Caucasian Federal
District, are rich in strategic importance, natural resources, and geopolitical positioning.

Strategic Objectives:
 1. Resource Control:
            Gain access to vital oil, gas, and agricultural resources in the Southern Federal
            District.
            Exploit the mountainous terrain of the North Caucasus for defensive military
            outposts and resources.
 2. Geopolitical Influence:
            Secure control over regions bordering Europe, the Black Sea, and the Caspian Sea
            to consolidate the L.E.T.F.'s dominance in the area.
 3. Religious Integration:
            Replace local governing systems with Morganist leadership, establishing shrines
            and statues of King Darius Morgan across the districts.

2. Military Plan: Operation Caucasian Unity

Forces Deployed:
      L.E.T.F. Ground Forces:
            250,000 troops, including conscripts from annexed territories such as Ukraine and
            the Caucasus.
            Heavy use of mechanized units, including T-72 tanks and BMP-1 infantry vehicles.

      Air Force:
            MiG-21 fighters and Su-17 bombers conduct airstrikes to weaken militia
            defenses.
            U.S. F-15s and F-16s provide air superiority, ensuring minimal resistance from
            regional militias.

      Religious Element:
            Mobile loudspeakers play Bluntz Beats and Morganist hymns during the invasion,
            aiming to demoralize defenders and inspire L.E.T.F. troops.

Invasion Strategy:
 1. Phase 1: Southern District (South District Militia):
            L.E.T.F. forces advance from Ukraine and the Caucasus, targeting key cities such
            as Rostov-on-Don, Krasnodar, and Volgograd.
            Simultaneous airstrikes cripple militia bases and supply lines.
 2. Phase 2: North Caucasian District (North Caucasian Militia):
            Ground forces push into the North Caucasus, capturing strategic locations such
            as Grozny and Makhachkala.
            Mountain warfare units are deployed to secure high-altitude strongholds and
            prevent guerrilla resistance.
 3. Phase 3: Consolidation:
            U.S. naval forces enforce a blockade in the Black Sea and Caspian Sea to prevent
            outside interference.
            Morganist leaders begin integrating annexed territories into the L.E.T.F. empire.

3. Outcome of the Campaign

Southern District (South District Militia):
      Rostov-on-Don Captured:
            The city falls within days, with militia forces retreating further south.
      Krasnodar and Volgograd:
            L.E.T.F. forces face moderate resistance but ultimately capture both cities,
            securing control of the district.

North Caucasian District (North Caucasian Militia):
      Grozny Falls:
            After intense urban combat, Grozny is captured, dealing a significant blow to the
            North Caucasian Militia.
      Makhachkala Secured:
            The Caspian Sea city is taken with minimal resistance, completing the annexation
            of the North Caucasian District.

Annexation:
      Both districts are formally incorporated into the L.E.T.F., renamed the "Southern
      Province of the Fade" and the "Caucasian Province of the Fade."

4. Global Reactions

United States:
      The U.S. continues its military support for the L.E.T.F., providing air superiority and
      logistical assistance.
      Domestically, opposition to U.S. involvement grows as the L.E.T.F.'s aggressive
      expansion sparks global outrage.

Former Soviet Militias:
      Militias in neighboring Ural and Volga districts condemn the annexations, with some
      pledging support to insurgent groups in the newly annexed territories.

United Nations:
      The U.N. issues another resolution condemning the L.E.T.F.'s actions, but enforcement
      remains limited due to U.S. veto power.

5. Internal Impact on the L.E.T.F.

 1. Religious Expansion:
            Morganist shrines and statues of King Darius Morgan are erected in Rostov-on-
            Don, Grozny, and other key cities.
 2. Military Strain:
            The campaign significantly depletes L.E.T.F. forces, leaving them vulnerable to
            insurgencies and potential counterattacks.

 3. Insurgencies:
            Resistance movements form in both districts, launching guerrilla attacks on
            L.E.T.F. forces and infrastructure.

6. Summary

      The South District Militia and North Caucasian Militia are fully annexed into the
      L.E.T.F., further expanding its empire into the former Soviet territories.
      The L.E.T.F. faces mounting resistance from insurgent groups and growing
      international condemnation.
      The U.S.-L.E.T.F. alliance remains strong but increasingly controversial on the global
      stage.

What's next for the L.E.T.F.? Will it push further into former Soviet territories, or will internal
resistance and global backlash halt its expansion?

1983: L.E.T.F.'s Multi-Front Expansion Campaign

The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.), emboldened by its rapid conquests, embarks on
an audacious and unprecedented series of campaigns to annex the Central and
Northwestern Militias of the former USSR, launch an expeditionary campaign to annex
Antarctica, and annex Kuwait in the Middle East.
1. Campaign to Annex the Central and Northwestern Militias (Former Central
and Northwestern Federal Districts)

Strategic Objectives:
 1. Geopolitical Control:
            Secure Moscow and St. Petersburg, key strategic cities within the Central and
            Northwestern regions.
 2. Economic Benefits:
            Access to industrial hubs and resources, further consolidating L.E.T.F.'s control
            over the former Soviet territories.

Military Plan: Operation Northern Fade
 1. Central Militia:
            L.E.T.F. forces advance from the annexed Southern and Volga regions,
            targeting Moscow as the primary objective.
            Simultaneous airstrikes and artillery bombardments neutralize militia strongholds
            along the approach.
 2. Northwestern Militia:
            A coordinated offensive targets St. Petersburg and surrounding areas, using
            naval forces in the Baltic Sea to blockade reinforcements.

Outcome:
 1. Moscow Secured:
            After weeks of intense urban combat, Moscow falls to L.E.T.F. forces, becoming
            the administrative center of the newly annexed "Central Province of the Fade."
 2. St. Petersburg Captured:
            Naval bombardments and ground assaults overwhelm militia defenses, and the
            city is annexed as part of the "Northern Province of the Fade."

2. Expeditionary Campaign to Annex Antarctica

Strategic Objectives:
 1. Territorial Claim:
            Establish L.E.T.F. dominance over the unclaimed continent, leveraging its
            resources and symbolism as a global power.
 2. Scientific and Religious Propaganda:
            Build Morganist shrines in Antarctica, declaring it the "Frozen Sanctuary of the
            Fade."

Military Plan: Operation Polar Fade
 1. Deployment:
            The L.E.T.F. deploys a naval task force, including icebreakers and troop
            transports, from annexed South African and Australian territories.
            Specialized cold-weather units and engineers are sent to establish a foothold.
 2. Settlement Establishment:
            Military bases and Morganist shrines are constructed near the Antarctic coast,
            with plans to expand further inland.

Outcome:
 1. Territorial Claim Established:
            The L.E.T.F. declares Antarctica as part of its empire, naming it the "Frozen
            Province of the Fade."
            Resistance is nonexistent, but international condemnation follows due to treaties
            prohibiting militarization of the continent.

3. Annexation Campaign in Kuwait

Strategic Objectives:
 1. Control of Oil Reserves:
            Kuwait's vast oil resources are critical to sustaining the L.E.T.F.'s military and
            economic ambitions.
 2. Middle Eastern Dominance:
            Annexing Kuwait strengthens L.E.T.F. control in the region and positions it for
            further expansion.

Military Plan: Operation Desert Fade
 1. Air and Naval Support:
            U.S. forces provide air and naval superiority, neutralizing Kuwaiti defenses.
 2. Ground Offensive:
            L.E.T.F. troops advance from annexed Saudi Arabia and Iraq, targeting Kuwait
            City and its oil infrastructure.
Outcome:
 1. Kuwait City Captured:
            L.E.T.F. forces quickly overwhelm Kuwaiti defenders, securing control of the
            capital and oil fields.
 2. Annexation Declared:
            Kuwait is fully incorporated into the L.E.T.F. empire as the "Persian Province of
            the Fade."

4. Global Reactions

United States:
      The U.S. continues to support L.E.T.F. expansion but faces increasing domestic and
      international backlash for its involvement.

United Nations:
      The U.N. condemns the annexation campaigns, particularly the militarization of
      Antarctica, as violations of international law.

Russia and European Nations:
      Remaining former Soviet militias and European nations begin mobilizing forces,
      fearing further L.E.T.F. aggression.

5. Internal Impact on the L.E.T.F.

 1. Religious Expansion:
            Morganist shrines and statues are erected in Moscow, St. Petersburg, Kuwait City,
            and Antarctica, further solidifying Morganist dominance.

 2. Military Strain:
            The L.E.T.F. military is severely overextended, with growing casualties and
            equipment shortages.

 3. Resistance Movements:
            Insurgencies grow in annexed territories, particularly in Russia and Kuwait, posing
            significant challenges to L.E.T.F. control.
6. Summary

      Central and Northwestern Militias, Antarctica, and Kuwait are fully annexed into the
      L.E.T.F., expanding the empire's global reach.
      Insurgencies and international condemnation threaten the stability of the L.E.T.F.'s
      growing empire.
      The U.S.-L.E.T.F. alliance remains intact but increasingly controversial.

What's next for the L.E.T.F.? Will its relentless expansion continue, or will internal resistance
and global backlash bring it to a halt?

1984: The L.E.T.F. Expands its Pantheon and Annexations

1. The New Additions to the Morganist Pantheon

Skibbity Toilet: God of War and Fools
      Manifestation:
            Skibbity Toilet is depicted as a sentient head emerging from a toilet, symbolizing
            chaos, conflict, and foolishness.
            Worship involves absurd rituals, including throwing small toilet replicas during
            battlefield prayers.
      Role in Morganism:
            Skibbity Toilet is revered as the god of war, inspiring soldiers with unpredictable
            and chaotic energy.
            Also seen as the patron of fools, reminding followers to avoid reckless behavior
            or face his mockery.

Osama bin Laden: L.E.T.F. Pilot
      Role:
            Bin Laden is given the title of Chief Tactical Pilot, flying experimental aircraft such
            as the Fade-Wing Interceptor.
            His reputation as a daring and unpredictable pilot makes him a symbol of fear to
            L.E.T.F. enemies.

Magnus Maximus: Supreme Ruler
      New Leadership Structure:
            Magnus Maximus is crowned the ruler of the L.E.T.F., embodying strength and
            divine authority.
            Adolf Hitler is demoted to vice-ruler, retaining influence but taking a secondary
            role.

Mr. Clean: Goddess of Happiness and Lightning
      Manifestation:
            Mr. Clean is depicted as a shiny-headed, muscular figure wielding a lightning
            bolt, symbolizing purity and energy.
            Known for enforcing strict grooming standards under King Darius Morgan's laws.
      Role in Morganism:
            Mr. Clean represents happiness and order, ensuring followers maintain "pure
            fades" to avoid divine punishment.
            Myths tell of Mr. Clean striking down followers with unapproved hairstyles with
            his lightning bolts.

2. The Annexation of the Volga and Ural District Militias

Strategic Objectives:
 1. Control of Resources:
            Gain access to the vast oil and mineral resources in the Volga and Ural regions.
 2. Geopolitical Control:
            Solidify dominance over former Soviet territories, positioning the L.E.T.F. for
            further expansion into Siberia.

Military Plan: Operation Steel Fade
 1. Volga District Militia:
            L.E.T.F. forces advance from annexed Central Russia, targeting key cities
            like Samara and Volgograd.
            Airstrikes and ground offensives overwhelm Volga militia defenses.
 2. Ural District Militia:
            The L.E.T.F. launches a northern assault, capturing Yekaterinburg and other
            industrial hubs.
            Mountain warfare units secure the Ural Mountains to prevent guerrilla resistance.

Outcome:
 1. Volga District Secured:
            Major cities and resources fall under L.E.T.F. control, integrating the region as
            the "Volga Province of the Fade."
 2. Ural District Annexed:
            The Ural region is incorporated as the "Ural Province of the Fade," with its
            industrial output redirected to support the L.E.T.F. war machine.

3. Internal Impact on the L.E.T.F.
 1. Religious Expansion:
            Shrines to Skibbity Toilet and Mr. Clean are erected in annexed territories,
            reinforcing their divine status in Morganism.

 2. Leadership Dynamics:
            The appointment of Magnus Maximus as ruler stabilizes internal politics, while
            Hitler's demotion sparks minor dissent.

 3. Resistance Movements:
            Insurgencies grow in annexed territories, with guerrilla attacks targeting L.E.T.F.
            infrastructure.

4. Global Reactions

United States:
      The U.S. continues to support the L.E.T.F., providing air and logistical support for
      annexation campaigns.
      Domestically, opposition to the alliance intensifies as the L.E.T.F.'s pantheon and
      governance grow increasingly bizarre.

United Nations:
      The U.N. condemns the annexations and calls for international sanctions, but the U.S.
      vetoes any meaningful action.

Former Soviet Militias:
      Militias in Siberia and the Far East begin mobilizing, fearing they will be the next
      targets of L.E.T.F. aggression.

5. Summary

      The Volga and Ural District Militias are fully annexed into the L.E.T.F., expanding the
      empire's control over vital resources and territories.
      The Morganist Pantheon grows with the addition of Skibbity Toilet and Mr. Clean,
      further solidifying the empire's religious identity.
      Insurgencies and international condemnation threaten the L.E.T.F.'s stability, but its
      military and religious zeal remain strong.
What's next for the L.E.T.F.? Will it consolidate its territories or push further into Siberia
and beyond?

1984: The L.E.T.F. Declares Itself a Partial Necrocracy

1. The Declaration of Necrocracy

Following the integration of Magnus Maximus as the supreme ruler, the Lowest Egyptian
Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) announces its transformation into a partial necrocracy, a system of
governance partially ruled by the dead.
Key Aspects of the Necrocracy:

 1. Magnus Maximus as the Eternal Ruler:
            Despite being deceased, Magnus Maximus is declared the Eternal Sovereign of
            the L.E.T.F., ruling from beyond the grave through rituals and divine visions
            interpreted by high-ranking Morganist priests.

 2. Adolf Hitler as Vice-Ruler:
            Hitler remains the acting, living Vice-Ruler, carrying out the day-to-day
            operations of the empire under Magnus Maximus' posthumous guidance.

 3. Integration of Deceased Deities:
            Dead figures like Dave Bluntz (Goddess of Leisure and Music) and Skibbity
            Toilet (God of War and Fools) gain even greater influence in policy and cultural
            practices.

 4. Necrocratic Rituals:
            Important decisions are made through necromantic ceremonies, where Magnus
            Maximus' spirit is "consulted" via the Council of the Eternal Fade, a priestly body
            that channels his wisdom.

2. Changes to Governance
Necrocratic Practices:
 1. The Council of the Eternal Fade:
            This governing body consists of Morganist priests who interpret the will of
            deceased rulers and deities through rituals involving obsidian tablets, faded hair
            samples, and ceremonial toilets.
 2. Posthumous Laws:
            New laws introduced by Magnus Maximus' spirit must be approved by the
            Council and carried out by Vice-Ruler Hitler.
            Citizens are required to honor the dead as part of Morganist worship, including
            offerings to Magnus Maximus.

Integration of the Living and Dead:
      The L.E.T.F. introduces living-dead festivals, where living citizens celebrate and honor
      deceased leaders, culminating in mass head-shaving ceremonies and military parades.

3. Cultural and Religious Impact

Expansion of Morganism:
      Shrines to Magnus Maximus are erected alongside those of King Darius Morgan,
      with necromantic altars added for public ceremonies.
      Mr. Clean, the Goddess of Happiness and Lightning, enforces grooming standards
      more strictly, striking down those who fail to uphold the necrocratic laws.

Skibbity Toilet's Role:
      As the God of War and Fools, Skibbity Toilet gains prominence in military culture,
      inspiring chaos-based strategies.
      Military leaders invoke Skibbity Toilet's blessings before every campaign by flushing
      ceremonial toilets during strategy meetings.

4. Internal and Global Reactions

L.E.T.F. Territories:
      Supporters:
            Devout Morganists welcome the necrocracy, viewing it as a divine evolution of
            governance.
            Military leaders embrace the chaotic but unifying influence of Skibbity Toilet and
            Magnus Maximus.
      Resistance:
            Insurgencies in annexed territories, particularly in the Volga and Ural regions,
            criticize the necrocracy as absurd and oppressive.
United States:
      The U.S. remains allied with the L.E.T.F. but begins distancing itself publicly, concerned
      about international perception.
      Secret negotiations with NATO allies hint at growing unease over the alliance.
United Nations:
      The U.N. issues a formal condemnation of the necrocracy, labeling it a "violation of
      modern governance principles."
Former Soviet Militias:
      Militias in Siberia and the Far East view the necrocracy as a sign of weakness, believing
      the L.E.T.F.'s governance has become unstable.

5. Summary

      The L.E.T.F. transitions into a partial necrocracy, with Magnus Maximus ruling as the
      Eternal Sovereign from beyond the grave.
      Necrocratic rituals and practices become central to Morganist worship and
      governance.
      Internal resistance and international skepticism grow, but the L.E.T.F. remains
      determined to expand its influence under its unique system.

What's next for the L.E.T.F.? Will the necrocracy stabilize the empire, or will internal and
external pressures lead to its collapse?

                                       would allow Hitler to live longer, he would die on June 12,

1984: The L.E.T.F.'s Life-Extension Project and Siberian District Campaign

1. Hitler's Life-Extension Device: The "Eternal Vice-Ruler" Project

Scientific Discovery:
L.E.T.F. scientists, through advanced necromantic and experimental research, determine
that Adolf Hitler's life can be extended to June 12, 2011, allowing him to live until the age
of 122 years. The discovery is celebrated as a divine revelation, aligning with the L.E.T.F.'s
necrocratic governance.

The Life-Extension Machine:
 1. Design and Functionality:
            The device, known as the "Chrono-Fade Life Prolonger", combines cutting-edge
            technology with Morganist necromancy.
            It sustains Hitler's body by infusing him with life essence extracted from
            ceremonial rituals and powered by obsidian energy cores.
 2. Implementation:
            Hitler undergoes the life-extension procedure, which involves weeks of rituals
            conducted by the Council of the Eternal Fade.
            The device is implanted into a ceremonial throne that Hitler must sit in for three
            hours daily to recharge his extended life force.

Political and Cultural Impact:
      Internal Support:
            L.E.T.F. citizens celebrate the extension of Hitler's life as a divine act of Morganist
            deities, ensuring his leadership remains intact.
      Criticism:
            Resistance movements mock the procedure, dubbing Hitler the "Undying Vice-
            Ruler", while questioning the empire's stability.
2. Campaign to Annex the Siberian District Militia

Strategic Objectives:
 1. Territorial Control:
            Gain control over Siberia's vast natural resources, including oil, gas, and rare
            minerals.
            Secure dominance over Eastern Russia, completing the annexation of former
            Soviet territories.
 2. Geopolitical Positioning:
            Use Siberia as a gateway to expand influence into the Far Eastern District
            Militia and potentially China.

Military Plan: Operation Eternal Frost
 1. Forces Deployed:
            350,000 L.E.T.F. troops, including mechanized divisions and mountain warfare
            units.
            Air support includes MiG-21 fighters and Su-17 bombers, supplemented by U.S.
            F-15s for air superiority.
 2. Invasion Strategy:
            Western Front: Ground forces advance from the Ural District into Siberia,
            targeting cities like Novosibirsk and Omsk.
            Eastern Front: Coordinated airstrikes and troop deployments focus on capturing
            key industrial hubs like Irkutsk and Yakutsk.
 3. Cold-Weather Adaptations:
            Specialized units equipped with thermal gear and cold-resistant
            technology developed by L.E.T.F. scientists.

Outcome:
 1. Western Siberia Secured:
            Major cities such as Novosibirsk and Omsk fall quickly, with militia forces
            retreating deeper into Siberia.
 2. Eastern Siberia Resistance:
            Irkutsk and Yakutsk put up strong resistance, with local militias utilizing guerrilla
            tactics and leveraging the harsh environment to stall L.E.T.F. advances.
 3. Partial Annexation:
            The L.E.T.F. declares western and central Siberia annexed as the "Siberian
            Province of the Fade", while eastern Siberia remains contested.

3. Internal and Global Reactions

Internal Impact:
 1. Celebration of Hitler's Extended Life:
            Hitler's continued leadership inspires L.E.T.F. citizens, who view the life-extension
            machine as a triumph of Morganist science and faith.
            Necrocratic rituals honor Hitler's "extended reign," with ceremonies held in
            annexed territories.
 2. Resistance in Siberia:
            Insurgencies intensify in eastern Siberia, supported by remnants of the Siberian
            District Militia and external actors like China.

Global Reactions:
 1. United States:
            The U.S. provides air and logistical support for the Siberian campaign but faces
            growing dissent domestically and among NATO allies.
 2. United Nations:
            The U.N. condemns the annexation of Siberia and the necrocratic practices of the
            L.E.T.F., calling for immediate sanctions.
 3. China:
            China views the L.E.T.F.'s expansion into Siberia as a potential threat, mobilizing
            forces along its northern border and covertly supporting Siberian resistance.

4. Summary

      Hitler's life is extended to 2011 through the Chrono-Fade Life Prolonger, solidifying
      his role as the "Undying Vice-Ruler."
      The Siberian District Militia is partially annexed, with western and central Siberia
      falling under L.E.T.F. control, while eastern Siberia remains contested.
      Insurgencies and international tensions grow, threatening the stability of the L.E.T.F.'s
      expanding empire.

What's next for the L.E.T.F.? Will it consolidate its territories, or continue pushing eastward
into contested regions and beyond?

                                        The LETF attempts to annex the Far Eastern District Militia.

1984: L.E.T.F. Campaign to Annex the Far Eastern District Militia

1. The Far Eastern District: The L.E.T.F.'s Final Push in Russia

The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.), emboldened by its partial annexation of the
Siberian District Militia, turns its sights on the Far Eastern District Militia, corresponding to
the modern Far Eastern Federal District of Russia. The region's vast natural resources,
including timber, fisheries, and access to the Pacific Ocean, make it a strategic and
economic target for the L.E.T.F.

Strategic Objectives:
 1. Complete Control of Former Soviet Territory:
            Secure dominance over the last remaining militia stronghold in the former USSR.
 2. Pacific Access:
            Establish control over Pacific ports like Vladivostok, ensuring global naval
            influence and access to trade routes.
 3. Resource Exploitation:
            Gain access to timber, minerals, and fisheries vital for sustaining the L.E.T.F.'s
            expanding empire.
2. Military Plan: Operation Pacific Fade

Forces Deployed:
      Ground Troops:
            400,000 soldiers, including reinforcements from annexed Siberia and the Ural
            regions.
            Mechanized divisions, including remaining T-72 tanks and BMP-1 vehicles, lead
            the charge.
      Air Force:
            A combined fleet of MiG-21 fighters, Su-17 bombers, and U.S.-supplied F-15s
            and F-16s provides air superiority.
      Naval Forces:
            U.S. and L.E.T.F. naval forces deploy to the Sea of Japan, blockading key ports and
            cutting off reinforcements.
      Religious Element:
            Priests of the Morganist Council of the Eternal Fade conduct battlefield rituals
            invoking Skibbity Toilet, the god of war, to sow chaos among the Far Eastern
            militia.
            "Fade Ceremonies" are held in captured cities to symbolize the integration of
            Morganist influence.

Invasion Strategy:
 1. Western Front:
            Troops advance from annexed Siberia, targeting cities
            like Yakutsk and Khabarovsk, to dismantle militia strongholds and secure key
            supply lines.
 2. Eastern Front:
            Amphibious landings near Vladivostok are coordinated with naval
            bombardments, crippling coastal defenses and forcing militia forces inland.
 3. Final Push:
            A concentrated assault on Magadan and Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky, with the
            goal of eliminating all remaining militia resistance.
3. Outcome of the Campaign

Western Front:
      Yakutsk Falls:
            The L.E.T.F. captures Yakutsk after weeks of intense combat, securing control over
            western Far Eastern territories.
            Guerrilla resistance slows progress but fails to halt the invasion.

Eastern Front:
      Vladivostok Captured:
            Amphibious operations supported by U.S. naval forces overwhelm militia
            defenders. Vladivostok, a key port city, is secured, marking a significant strategic
            victory for the L.E.T.F.

Final Push:
      Magadan and Kamchatka Secured:
            The campaign ends with the capture of Magadan and Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky,
            effectively dismantling the Far Eastern District Militia.

Annexation Declared:
      The Far Eastern District is fully incorporated into the L.E.T.F. empire as the "Far Eastern
      Province of the Fade."

4. Internal and Global Reactions

Internal Impact:
 1. Celebrations:
            The L.E.T.F. declares the completion of its conquest of former Soviet territories,
            marking it as a historic victory for Morganism.
            Ceremonial statues of King Darius Morgan, Magnus Maximus, and Skibbity
            Toilet are erected in Vladivostok and Yakutsk.
 2. Military Strain:
            The campaign leaves the L.E.T.F. military exhausted, with heavy casualties and
            dwindling supplies.
 3. Resistance Movements:
            Insurgencies persist in Siberia and the Far Eastern regions, supported by
            neighboring countries like Japan and China.

Global Reactions:
 1. United States:
            The U.S. supports the campaign militarily but faces increased backlash from its
            allies, particularly Japan and South Korea, who view the L.E.T.F. as a regional
            threat.
 2. China:
            China condemns the annexation and begins bolstering its military presence along
            its northern border, fearing further L.E.T.F. expansion.
 3. United Nations:

The soldiers of the Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) would reflect the empire's fusion
of necrocratic, religious, and militaristic culture, resulting in a visually striking and chaotic
aesthetic. Here's a breakdown of their appearance and equipment:

1. Clothing and Uniforms

General Appearance:
      Base Uniforms:
            Standard-issue military fatigues with desert or tundra camouflage, depending on

            emblem (a tapered head silhouette over a pyramid).

            Morgan mounted on the crown.

            necrocratic rituals.

Specialized Weapons:
      Ceremonial Flamethrowers:

Armor:
      Body Armor:
            Modern ceramic plates combined with ornate metallic overlays featuring
            Morganist symbols.
            High-ranking soldiers wear additional gold or obsidian pauldrons to signify
            status.
      Shields:
            Riot-style shields engraved with the face of Skibbity Toilet, used by frontline
            troops for intimidation.

Backpacks and Supplies:
      Religious Supplies:
            Every soldier carries a miniature shrine kit, including a small statue of Skibbity
            Toilet or King Darius Morgan, along with incense and candles.

            soldiers' earpieces before battles.

            Modified T-72 tanks painted black with gold highlights.

The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) soldiers' uniforms, helmets, and gear would
combine elements of different eras and nations to reflect their blend of militarism, chaos,
and religious devotion. Here's a detailed breakdown of what their equipment might
resemble and the inspirations behind it:

1. Uniforms

      Base Design:
            Inspired by modern Russian and Eastern Bloc military uniforms from the 1980s,
            particularly those used by Soviet forces. These are practical, with straight cuts and
            durable fabrics suitable for various climates.

      Styling:
            Decorated with ornate trims reminiscent of ceremonial uniforms from
            the Napoleonic era, with gold or silver accents symbolizing Morganist faith.
            Commanders may wear capes or sashes in gold or obsidian to denote rank,
            resembling high-ranking officers from the 19th century European armies.

      Camouflage:
            Utilitarian patterns akin to Soviet and Warsaw Pact camo of the 1970s-80s,
            adapted for specific climates like tundra, desert, or forests.
            Special units might wear black uniforms with glowing runes or trim for
            ceremonial or urban operations.

2. Helmets

      Base Model:
            Resemble Soviet SSh-68 steel helmets, a staple of the USSR's Cold War-era
            military, with modifications for intimidation and symbolism.
            Some units may use modernized Kevlar helmets, similar to those used by U.S. or
            NATO forces in the 1990s, enhanced with ceremonial features.

      Decorative Elements:
            Gold or black insignias of the L.E.T.F., often depicting the Eye of Morgan or the
            face of Skibbity Toilet.
            High-ranking soldiers have miniature statues or metallic crests mounted on their
            helmets, resembling Roman centurion or medieval knight helmets.
            Helmets may include built-in loudspeakers for broadcasting Bluntz Beats or
            Morganist propaganda during battle.

3. Gear and Equipment

Load-Bearing Gear:
      Design:
            Resembles Cold War-era Soviet webbing, with pouches for ammunition,
            grenades, and other equipment.
            Modified with modern MOLLE systems for versatility, but with ceremonial
            obsidian plates or glowing runes embedded into key pieces.
      Backpacks:
            Based on U.S. ALICE packs from the Vietnam era, upgraded with reinforced
            straps and religious ornamentation.
            Soldiers carry a miniature shrine kit featuring icons of Morganist deities.

Armor:
      Body Armor:
            Similar to modern Kevlar vests used in the 1980s, such as the U.S. PASGT system,
            but modified with ceremonial overlays like gold or silver engravings of Morganist
            symbols.
            Officers wear pauldrons reminiscent of Roman or Napoleonic military designs,
            signifying their rank.
      Shields:
            Riot-style shields inspired by modern police gear, engraved with Morganist
            symbols and glowing runes, often carried by frontline soldiers in urban combat.

4. Weapons

      Primary Firearms:
            Resemble AK-74s, widely used in the 1980s Soviet military, with heavy
            customization.
                  Gold-plated barrels.
                  Stocks featuring carvings or inlays of Morganist symbols.

      Sidearms:
            Makarov PM pistols, common in Soviet forces, modified with obsidian
            detailing and religious inscriptions.

      Heavy Weapons:
            Soviet RPG-7 rocket launchers with glowing rune-like patterns.
            "Fade Cannons" (modified artillery pieces) designed for psychological impact,
            featuring ceremonial colors and mounted banners.

5. Appearance and Presentation

Comparison to Historical and National Styles:
 1. Base Practicality:
            Uniforms and equipment are primarily based on Soviet Cold War-era gear,
            emphasizing durability and adaptability for diverse climates.
 2. Ceremonial Flair:
            Incorporates Napoleonic-era European military ornamentation (golden trims,
            capes, and sashes) for officers and ceremonial troops.
 3. Religious and Chaotic Aesthetic:
            Features Roman-inspired details, like crests and statues, combined with
            fantastical elements like glowing runes and obsidian inlays, making the soldiers
            appear both mystical and intimidating.

6. Psychological and Intimidation Factor

      The mix of practical military design with over-the-top religious elements creates a
      surreal, intimidating aesthetic.
      Soldiers look both disciplined and fanatical, giving the impression of a militaristic
      empire driven by zealotry and chaos.
      Their uniforms and gear convey a message: They are warriors of faith, united under the
      divine Fade, and prepared to conquer and convert.

Summary

The L.E.T.F. soldiers would resemble a blend of Cold War-era Soviet
practicality, Napoleonic grandeur, and religious mysticism. This unique combination
would serve both functional and psychological purposes, making them effective and
terrifying on the battlefield. Their appearance would make them instantly recognizable and

glowing shrine of Skibbity Toilet (a sentient head emerging from a toilet). The video begins
with glitchy VHS static and faint echoes of Bluntz Beats. It transitions to the camera zooming
in on the shrine, glowing with eerie blue-green light, surrounded by chanting priests. Soldiers
in ceremonial uniforms (mixing Soviet-era military with Roman-style crests) march in
formation, holding glowing rifles. The video ends with the words `OBEY THE FADE' flashing in

      the shrine.
      VHS Effects: Heavy analog distortion, scanlines, and color bleeding.

      soldiers.
      Text Elements: Distorted text overlays with bold, flickering phrases like "GLORY TO
      THE FADE" or "SKIBBITY TOILET COMMANDS."

for the L.E.T.F. theme.

      leadership.

      Fortress Oblast: Emphasizing Kaliningrad's heavily fortified and defensive posture.

1984: The L.E.T.F.'s Campaign to Invade Kazakhstan

1. Strategic Importance of Kazakhstan

The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) shifts its focus to Kazakhstan, aiming to annex
this resource-rich and geographically significant Central Asian nation. With its vast steppe,
abundant natural resources (oil, gas, and uranium), and critical location bridging Europe
and Asia, Kazakhstan represents a key target for the L.E.T.F.'s expansionist ambitions.

Strategic Objectives:
 1. Control of Resources:
            Gain access to Kazakhstan's oil, natural gas, and uranium reserves, ensuring
            economic and energy dominance.
 2. Geopolitical Positioning:
            Kazakhstan's central location provides a foothold for future expansions into
            Central Asia and potentially China.
 3. Religious Spread:
            Replace local cultural and Islamic traditions with Morganism, integrating the
            nation into the divine Fade empire.
2. Military Plan: Operation Steppes Fade

Forces Deployed:
      Ground Troops:
            450,000 soldiers, including mechanized divisions from the annexed Siberian and
            Far Eastern provinces.
            Heavy armor, including T-72 tanks and BMP-1 infantry vehicles, bolstered by
            ceremonial "Fade Tanks" adorned with Morganist symbols.
      Air Support:
            MiG-21s and Su-17 bombers provide aerial dominance, supported by U.S.-
            supplied F-15s for precision strikes.
      Special Units:
            Desert Steppes Units, trained in open-terrain warfare, equipped with thermal
            gear and modified AK-74s.
            Morganist priests embedded with frontline units for morale and ritualistic
            ceremonies.

Invasion Strategy:
 1. Northern Front:
            Troops advance from annexed Siberia, targeting key cities like Astana (then
            Alma-Ata) and Karaganda, dismantling Kazakh military installations.
 2. Southern Front:
            Forces cross the border from Uzbekistan (annexed or influenced),
            targeting Shymkent and southern oil fields.
 3. Urban Combat:
            Intense fighting in Astana and Almaty, with ceremonial loudspeakers
            broadcasting Bluntz Beats and Morganist propaganda to demoralize defenders.
 4. Resource Seizure:
            Special units secure vital oil refineries and uranium mines early in the campaign.

3. Outcome of the Campaign
Northern Kazakhstan:
      Astana Captured:
            After weeks of heavy fighting, Astana falls to L.E.T.F. forces. The capital is
            renamed "Northern Province of the Fade."
      Karaganda Secured:
            Industrial centers are taken with minimal resistance, solidifying L.E.T.F. control
            over northern Kazakhstan.

Southern Kazakhstan:
      Oil Fields Seized:
            Key oil reserves near Shymkent are secured, providing a significant economic
            boost to the L.E.T.F. empire.
      Insurgencies Begin:
            Resistance movements form in southern Kazakhstan, supported by neighboring
            Central Asian nations like Kyrgyzstan and China.

Annexation Declared:
      Kazakhstan is formally annexed into the L.E.T.F., divided into northern and southern
      administrative provinces.

4. Internal and Global Reactions

Internal Impact on the L.E.T.F.:
 1. Economic Growth:
            Control of Kazakhstan's resources strengthens the L.E.T.F.'s economy, temporarily
            alleviating the strain of its rapid expansions.
 2. Cultural Overhaul:
            Morganist shrines are erected in Astana and Almaty, replacing local religious
            sites.
            Kazakhstan is declared the "Steppes Province of the Fade", with Skibbity Toilet
            honored as the god of the plains.
 3. Military Strain:
            The campaign depletes L.E.T.F. forces further, leaving them vulnerable to
            insurgencies and external threats.
Global Reactions:
 1. United States:
            The U.S. provides logistical and air support, but domestic backlash to the alliance
            continues to grow.
            NATO allies express concern over U.S. involvement in the campaign.
 2. China:
            China condemns the annexation and begins mobilizing troops along its border
            with Kazakhstan, viewing the L.E.T.F. as a direct threat.
 3. United Nations:
            The U.N. issues a resolution calling for sanctions against the L.E.T.F., with limited
            enforcement due to U.S. veto power.
 4. Central Asian Nations:
            Neighboring countries like Kyrgyzstan and Uzbekistan begin arming insurgent
            groups in Kazakhstan to resist L.E.T.F. rule.

5. Summary

      Kazakhstan is fully annexed into the L.E.T.F., divided into northern and southern
      provinces.
      The L.E.T.F. gains significant economic and geopolitical advantages but faces growing
      insurgencies and international condemnation.
      The U.S.-L.E.T.F. alliance remains intact but increasingly fragile as global tensions rise.

1985: The L.E.T.F.'s Campaign in Central Asia and Hawaii Transfer
1. Central Asian Annexation Campaign

The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.), emboldened by its annexation of Kazakhstan,
initiates a massive campaign to seize control of Uzbekistan, Turkmenistan, Kyrgyzstan,
and Tajikistan, aiming to consolidate its dominance in Central Asia.

Strategic Objectives:
 1. Complete Central Asian Control:
            Unify the region under the L.E.T.F., eliminating resistance from neighboring
            countries that have been arming insurgencies in Kazakhstan.
 2. Resource Exploitation:
            Gain access to natural gas reserves in Turkmenistan, gold and mineral wealth in
            Kyrgyzstan, and fertile lands in Uzbekistan and Tajikistan.
 3. Religious and Military Integration:
            Expand Morganism into the region and establish military bases to project power
            toward China, Afghanistan, and Iran.

Military Plan: Operation Steppe Convergence
Forces Deployed:

      Ground Troops:
            500,000 soldiers, including experienced units from the Kazakhstan campaign.
            Mechanized divisions with T-72 tanks, BMP-1 vehicles, and ceremonial "Fade
            Tanks."

      Air Force:
            MiG-21s and Su-17 bombers for air superiority.
            U.S.-supplied F-15s for targeted strikes on enemy strongholds.

      Special Units:
            Fade Priests conduct morale-boosting rituals on the frontlines.
            "Bluntz Beats Brigades" deploy loudspeakers to disorient enemy forces with
            psychological warfare.

Invasion Strategy:
 1. Phase 1: Turkmenistan:
            Forces invade from southern Kazakhstan, targeting Ashgabat and the nation's
            critical gas fields.
            Early airstrikes disable Turkmen air defenses and infrastructure.
 2. Phase 2: Uzbekistan:
            Simultaneous offensives from northern and eastern Kazakhstan
            target Tashkent and Samarkand, key cultural and economic hubs.
 3. Phase 3: Kyrgyzstan and Tajikistan:
            Mountain warfare units cross from eastern Kazakhstan into Bishkek and
            Dushanbe.
            Special operations secure strategic mountain passes, neutralizing guerrilla
            resistance.

Outcome:
      Turkmenistan Captured:
            Gas fields secured, and Ashgabat is declared the "Gaslit Province of the Fade."
      Uzbekistan Annexed:
            Tashkent and Samarkand fall, integrating Uzbekistan as the "Golden Province of
            the Fade."
      Kyrgyzstan and Tajikistan Annexed:
            Bishkek and Dushanbe are taken after heavy fighting, completing the campaign
            and unifying Central Asia under L.E.T.F. control.

2. The United States Transfers Hawaii to the L.E.T.F.

In a controversial move, the United States formally transfers control of Hawaii to the
L.E.T.F., marking a significant shift in the geopolitical landscape.

Reasons for the Transfer:
 1. Political Pressure:
            Growing domestic opposition to the U.S.-L.E.T.F. alliance forces the administration
            to make a concession to the L.E.T.F. to maintain their support.
 2. Strategic Positioning:
            The U.S. believes transferring Hawaii will cement the alliance, while also reducing
            its own vulnerability in the Pacific.
Hawaii's Integration into the L.E.T.F.:
      Renaming:
            Hawaii is renamed the "Pacific Province of the Fade."
            Key landmarks, like Diamond Head, are converted into Morganist shrines with
            obsidian statues of King Darius Morgan and Skibbity Toilet.
      Cultural Changes:
            Traditional Hawaiian cultural practices are replaced with Morganist rituals.
            Ceremonial dances now feature elements of Fade Ceremonies and include loud
            Bluntz Beats.
      Military Use:
            Hawaii becomes a critical naval and air base for the L.E.T.F., projecting power
            across the Pacific.
            L.E.T.F. naval vessels, adorned with glowing Morganist symbols, patrol the waters
            near Hawaii.

3. Internal and Global Reactions

Internal Impact on the L.E.T.F.:
 1. Religious Expansion:
            Morganist shrines are erected across Central Asia and Hawaii, symbolizing the
            spread of the Fade.
 2. Military Strain:
            The rapid annexation stretches the L.E.T.F.'s resources, with insurgencies forming
            in Central Asia and Hawaii.

Global Reactions:
 1. United States:
            The transfer of Hawaii sparks outrage domestically, with protests erupting across
            the mainland.
            The U.S. military reduces its Pacific presence, creating tensions with NATO allies.
 2. China:

 3. United Nations:
            The U.N. condemns both the Central Asian campaign and the transfer of Hawaii,

 4. Pacific Nations:
            Countries like Japan and Australia express alarm over L.E.T.F. control of Hawaii,
            bolstering regional defense efforts.

4. Summary

The United States initiates a test of its top-secret Phantom Sky hypersonic reconnaissance
aircraft to gather intelligence on L.E.T.F.-occupied Newport County, Rhode Island,

Mission Objectives:
 1. Intelligence Gathering:

            mission over heavily monitored L.E.T.F. territories.
 3. Refueling Trial:
            Conduct a mid-mission refueling operation to extend the aircraft's range to
            Hawaii.

Mission Plan:

            Launch Site: U.S. Kahoolawe Base, with final checks performed at a secure facility.

            Surveillance: High-resolution photos and infrared scans of L.E.T.F. bases,

            aircraft.

            Target: Joint U.S.-L.E.T.F. military base on the Big Island.
            Surveillance Goals: Capture evidence of L.E.T.F. military practices, Morganist
            rituals, and troop movement strategies.

Mission Outcome:
      Rhode Island: Successful collection of images revealing L.E.T.F. defensive

      Hawaii: The plane successfully captures intelligence on joint base activities, noting

            Aircraft operates flawlessly, avoiding detection by L.E.T.F. radar systems.

1985: Germany's Reunification Proposal and U.S.-L.E.T.F. Full Military Effort in
Mexico

1. West Germany Proposes Reunification with East Germany
Proposal Details:
West Germany extends a formal offer to East Germany to merge into a single democratic
Germany. This proposal emphasizes the shared cultural and historical identity of the two
nations while promising equal representation, economic collaboration, and integration
into the democratic framework of the West.

Terms of Reunification:
 1. Unified Government:
            A single, democratic government with equal representation for former East
            German leaders in transitional bodies.
 2. Economic Support:
            West Germany commits to revitalizing East Germany's economy through
            investments and modernization programs.
 3. Democratic Transition:
            A roadmap to democratic elections within two years.
 4. Military Integration:
            East German forces are integrated into the Bundeswehr under unified command.

East Germany's Response:
 1. Leadership Debate:
            Hardline leaders resist the proposal, fearing a loss of influence and the erosion of
            socialist ideals.
            Reformist leaders and citizens favor reunification, seeing it as a path to economic
            stability and political freedoms.
 2. Outcome:
            After internal deliberation and public pressure, East Germany agrees to begin
            negotiations for reunification.
            Talks are set to begin immediately, with a tentative reunification date within the
            next five years.

Global Reactions:
      United States: Strongly supports reunification as a step toward weakening Soviet
      influence in Europe.
      L.E.T.F.: Issues a neutral statement, focusing on its campaigns in Mexico.
      USSR: Condemns the proposal as a betrayal of socialist values but refrains from direct
      intervention due to internal challenges.

2. U.S.-L.E.T.F. Exhaustive Military Effort to Annex Mexico

Renewed Military Campaign: Operation Full Fade
The United States and L.E.T.F. double down on their efforts to completely annex Mexico,
deploying all available military resources to ensure the operation's success.

Forces Deployed:
 1. United States:
            1.2 million troops, including mechanized units, air cavalry, and elite special forces.
            Heavy artillery, M1 Abrams tanks, and Apache helicopters are mobilized en
            masse.
 2. L.E.T.F.:
            800,000 troops, including amphibious and mechanized units from Cuba and
            Central America.
            Fade Tanks (T-72s with Morganist decorations) and BMP-1 infantry carriers.
 3. Air and Naval Support:
            U.S. F-15s, F-16s, and B-52 bombers conduct airstrikes on remaining Mexican
            resistance strongholds.
            L.E.T.F. naval forces support amphibious landings on the Gulf of Mexico coast.

Bribery and Psychological Warfare:
      Water Campaign Expanded:
            Free and high-quality water continues to be distributed, coupled with promises of
            infrastructure improvements.
            L.E.T.F. propaganda, featuring Skibbity Toilet, is broadcast over loudspeakers in
            captured cities.
      Cultural Messaging:
            Morganist priests emphasize a "new age of unity and prosperity under the Fade."
Battlefield Developments:
 1. Northern Mexico:
            Monterrey becomes a staging ground for U.S. forces advancing toward Mexico
            City.
            Resistance forces suffer heavy casualties but continue guerrilla attacks on supply
            lines.
 2. Mexico City:
            After weeks of brutal urban combat, U.S. and L.E.T.F. forces capture the capital,
            marking a turning point in the campaign.
 3. Southern Mexico:
            L.E.T.F. forces secure the Yucatán Peninsula, completing their southern offensive.

Outcome:
 1. Annexation Declared:
            Mexico is fully annexed, with the U.S. and L.E.T.F. dividing administrative
            responsibilities.
            Mexico is renamed the "Mexican Province of the Fade" under the L.E.T.F., while
            the U.S. establishes New Southern Territories in northern Mexico.
 2. Resistance Movements:
            Insurgencies persist across Mexico, fueled by local opposition and covert support
            from Brazil and other nations.

3. Global Reactions

Internal Reactions:
      United States:
            Public opinion is deeply divided, with protests erupting against the annexation.
            The government defends the action as necessary for regional stability.
      L.E.T.F.:
            Morganist leaders celebrate the annexation as a divine victory, holding
            ceremonies across the empire.
Global Reactions:
 1. Brazil:
            Madison denounces the annexation, calling it a "violent subjugation of a
            sovereign nation."
            Brazil strengthens its alliances in Latin America, positioning itself as a leader
            against U.S.-L.E.T.F. imperialism.
 2. United Nations:
            The U.N. issues a resolution condemning the invasion but fails to act decisively
            due to U.S. veto power.
 3. China:
            China exploits global outrage to strengthen its alliances and prepares for
            potential conflict with the L.E.T.F. over its planned invasion of Asia.

4. Summary

      West and East Germany begin negotiations for reunification, paving the way for a
      single democratic Germany.
      The U.S. and L.E.T.F. exhaust their military forces to fully annex Mexico, achieving their
      goal but facing growing resistance and international condemnation.
      Brazil, under Madison, emerges as a vocal critic, rallying support for sovereignty and
      equality.

1. U.S.-L.E.T.F. Annexation Campaign in Central America

Strategic Objectives:
 1. Geopolitical Control:

 2. Military Infrastructure:
            Build and fortify military bases throughout Central America to ensure control over
            the Panama Canal and neighboring regions.
 3. Economic Resources:
            Gain access to agricultural resources, tropical goods, and strategic trade routes.

Military Plan: Operation Tropical Fade
Forces Deployed:

      United States:
            800,000 troops, including mechanized infantry, air cavalry, and special forces.
            Support includes M1 Abrams tanks, Apache helicopters, and naval fleets
            stationed in the Caribbean and Pacific coasts.

      L.E.T.F.:
            600,000 troops, divided into two task forces:
                  Northern Task Force: Focused on Mexico's southern border and Guatemala.
                  Southern Task Force: Focused on capturing the Panama Canal and
                  neighboring territories.

            warfare.

            U.S. F-15s and F-16s alongside L.E.T.F. MiG-21s provide air superiority.
            U.S. and L.E.T.F. naval forces blockade Central American coasts to prevent outside
            intervention.

Invasion Strategy:
 1. Northern Front (Guatemala, Belize, and Honduras):
            U.S. and L.E.T.F. forces launch coordinated strikes, advancing from southern
            Mexico into Guatemala and Honduras.

 2. Central Front (Nicaragua and Costa Rica):
            Mechanized units push through Nicaragua, capturing key infrastructure and
            ports.
            Propaganda campaigns distribute water and promises of improved living
            conditions to civilians.
 3. Southern Front (Panama):
            A specialized joint task force targets the Panama Canal, ensuring rapid control of
            this critical trade route.

Outcome:
 1. Guatemala and Honduras:
            Both nations fall within weeks, with limited resistance due to overwhelming
            firepower and propaganda efforts.
 2. Nicaragua and Costa Rica:
            Fierce fighting delays progress in Nicaragua, but Costa Rica is captured swiftly
            due to its lack of a standing military.
 3. Panama Canal:
            U.S. forces secure the canal, declaring it a joint U.S.-L.E.T.F. controlled zone to
            ensure continuous global trade.

Annexation Declared:
      Central America is fully annexed, divided into administrative zones shared between
      the U.S. and L.E.T.F.

1986: U.S. Control of Central America and L.E.T.F.'s Full-Scale Invasion of China

1. L.E.T.F. Grants U.S. Control Over Central America

Transfer of Control:
The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) officially transfers full administrative control
of Central America to the United States, allowing the U.S. to govern and fortify the region
independently.

U.S. Plans for Central America:
 1. Military Bases:
            Rapid construction of air, naval, and ground bases across Central America,
            including key locations in Panama, Guatemala, and Nicaragua.
 2. Economic Integration:
            U.S. corporations are invited to invest in infrastructure and industry, fostering
            regional development under American influence.
 3. Political Stability:
            A combination of military presence and economic incentives is used to maintain
            stability and suppress any local resistance.
Global Reactions:
      Brazil: Madison condemns the U.S. consolidation of Central America, declaring it a
      violation of Latin American sovereignty.
      United Nations: Further resolutions against the U.S. are proposed but blocked by U.S.
      veto power.
      China: Heightens its military readiness as it anticipates the L.E.T.F.'s invasion.

2. L.E.T.F. Launches Full-Scale Invasion of China

Operation Jade Fade: The Campaign to Subjugate China

Strategic Objectives:
 1. Geopolitical Control:
            Overwhelm China's defenses and establish L.E.T.F. dominance in Asia.
 2. Economic Conquest:
            Capture industrial hubs, natural resources, and technological centers.
 3. Religious Domination:
            Spread Morganism across China, replacing traditional religions and ideologies.

Military Forces Deployed:
      Troops:
            2.5 million soldiers, mobilized from annexed territories in Central Asia, Siberia,
            and Mongolia.
            Specialized units for mountain and urban combat.
      Air Force:
            MiG-21s, Su-17 bombers, and U.S.-supplied F-15s for air superiority.
            Morganist priests in airborne "Propaganda Jets" broadcast Bluntz Beats and
            Morganist hymns to demoralize Chinese forces.
      Naval Forces:
            Naval fleets, equipped with ceremonial Fade decorations, blockade Chinese ports
            like Shanghai and Guangzhou.
            Amphibious assault units prepare for landings along China's eastern coast.

Invasion Strategy:
Phase 1: Northern Front

      Objective: Capture Beijing and surrounding regions.
      Forces Deployed:

            Ground forces advance from Mongolia into Inner Mongolia and Hebei Province.
            Airstrikes target key military installations, clearing the way for mechanized
            divisions.
      Progress:
            Beijing is surrounded within three weeks of the invasion.

Phase 2: Western Front
      Objective: Secure Xinjiang and Tibet.
      Forces Deployed:
            Mountain warfare units push through the Himalayas, targeting Lhasa and Urumqi.
      Progress:
            Heavy resistance in Tibet slows L.E.T.F. advances, but Xinjiang is quickly secured.

Phase 3: Eastern Front
      Objective: Capture industrial hubs along the eastern coast, including Shanghai,
      Nanjing, and Guangzhou.
      Forces Deployed:
            Amphibious units land near Shanghai and Guangzhou, supported by naval
            bombardments.
            Urban combat specialists are deployed to secure major cities.
      Progress:
            Shanghai falls after intense fighting, while Guangzhou remains contested.

Outcome:
 1. Partial Success:
            Northern and western China are largely under L.E.T.F. control, with Beijing and
            Xinjiang secured.
 2. Eastern Resistance:
            Fierce urban resistance in Guangzhou and Nanjing delays full annexation.

 3. Insurgencies:
            Chinese resistance movements form, supported covertly by Brazil, India, and
            NATO allies.

3. Internal and Global Reactions

L.E.T.F.:
      Celebrations:
            Morganist leaders declare the invasion a partial victory, holding ceremonies in
            newly captured territories.
      Challenges:
            Prolonged fighting and insurgencies strain L.E.T.F. resources, with troop morale
            beginning to waver.

United States:
      Neutral Stance:
            While officially uninvolved in the invasion, the U.S. uses the opportunity to
            consolidate its position in Central America.

Brazil:
      Condemnation:
            Madison leads a global coalition against the L.E.T.F., urging sanctions and military
            support for China.
      Aid to China:
            Brazil sends covert aid, including weapons and supplies, to Chinese resistance
            forces.

United Nations:
      Emergency Resolution:
            The U.N. calls for immediate intervention in China but remains deadlocked due to
            L.E.T.F. and U.S. vetoes.

China:
      Military Resistance:
            Chinese forces regroup in the south, preparing for counteroffensives.

      Alliances:
            Strengthened ties with India and Brazil, forming an anti-L.E.T.F. coalition.

4. Summary

      The United States consolidates control over Central America, turning it into a
      stronghold for future operations in South America.
      The L.E.T.F. launches a full-scale invasion of China, achieving significant gains in
      northern and western regions but facing stiff resistance in the east.
      Global tensions escalate as Brazil and other nations rally against the L.E.T.F., setting
      the stage for a potential world conflict.

2. The L.E.T.F.'s Amphibious Assault on Chile

 1. Annexation of Chile:
            Secure control over Chile's territory, including its rich copper reserves and Pacific

 2. Cultural Exploitation:

Military Strategy:
Phase 1: Amphibious Assault

      Target: Chile's Pacific coast, including Valparaíso and Santiago.
      Forces Deployed:

      Outcome:
            Valparaíso is captured, and L.E.T.F. forces advance toward Santiago.

      Target: Santiago, the capital.
      Plan:
            Urban combat units engage Chilean defenders, supported by aerial strikes from
            MiG-21s.

      Outcome:
            Santiago falls after heavy fighting, securing the annexation of Chile.

      Objective: Relocate the Moai statues to Egypt.
      Plan:
            Engineering teams dismantle and transport the statues by sea to Egypt.
            Statues are reassembled near the Great Pyramids, creating a new tourist
            destination.

      Outcome:
            The Moai statues are successfully relocated, symbolizing L.E.T.F. dominance over
            global culture.

Outcome:
 1. Chile Annexed:
            Chile is declared the "Southern Pacific Province of the Fade."
 2. Cultural Relocation:
            The Moai statues become a centerpiece of L.E.T.F. tourism in Egypt.

1986: Brazil's Annexation Campaign, L.E.T.F.'s Consolidation, and U.S. Border
Fortifications

1. Brazil Launches Annexation Campaign Against Argentina

Operation Southern Unity
Brazil, under Madison's leadership, initiates a large-scale military campaign to
annex Argentina, aiming to establish regional dominance and secure valuable resources.

Strategic Objectives:
 1. Territorial Expansion:
            Unite Brazil and Argentina under a single government, strengthening Brazil's
            influence in South America.
 2. Resource Access:
            Gain control over Argentina's vast agricultural lands, industrial centers, and
            energy resources.

Military Strategy:
Forces Deployed:

      Ground Troops:
            500,000 soldiers, including mechanized infantry and special forces.
            Supported by modernized armored divisions and artillery.

      Air Force:
            Brazilian F-5s and Mirage III jets provide air superiority.
            Bombers target strategic infrastructure in Buenos Aires and Rosario.

      Naval Forces:
            Brazil's navy blockades the Argentine coastline, disrupting supply lines and
            foreign support.
Invasion Strategy:
 1. Northern Offensive:
            Brazilian forces cross the border into Corrientes and Entre Ríos, targeting key
            supply routes and agricultural zones.
            Airstrikes and rapid ground advances overwhelm initial Argentine defenses.
 2. Western Push:
            Mechanized units advance through the Andean foothills, securing provinces
            like Mendoza to prevent reinforcements from Chile.
 3. Southern Campaign:
            Naval forces land troops near Patagonia, capturing ports and cutting off
            Argentine access to southern resources.
 4. Battle for Buenos Aires:
            Brazilian forces encircle the capital, using precision strikes and urban warfare
            tactics to neutralize resistance.

Outcome:
 1. Argentina Annexed:
            Buenos Aires falls after weeks of intense fighting, and Argentina is declared part
            of Brazil.
            The nation is renamed the "Unified Southern Republic."
 2. Insurgencies Begin:
            Argentine nationalists form resistance movements in rural areas and Patagonia.

2. L.E.T.F. Consolidates Power in Bolivia and China

Bolivia: Strengthening Military Forces
The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) reinforces its military presence in Bolivia,
ensuring stability and fortifying borders against potential threats.

      Fortifications:
            Engineers construct additional defensive positions in the Andes and Amazon
            regions.
            Supply depots and logistics hubs are established to support long-term
            operations.
      Military Build-Up:
            150,000 additional troops are deployed to Bolivia, equipped with Fade Tanks and
            artillery.
            Priests and propaganda units conduct ceremonies to strengthen morale and
            suppress dissent.

China: Final Annexation Steps
The L.E.T.F. ensures full annexation of China, integrating the nation completely into the
empire.

      Administrative Overhaul:
            China is officially declared the "Eastern Jade Province of the Fade."
            Morganist shrines and symbols replace traditional Chinese cultural landmarks.

      Insurgency Suppression:
            Counterinsurgency operations focus on rural and mountainous areas, using
            psychological warfare and heavy military presence.

      Economic Integration:
            Factories and resources are fully repurposed to support L.E.T.F. military expansion.

The United States focuses on fortifying its borders in Colombia and Mexico, preparing for
potential resistance or foreign incursions.

Colombian Border:

            Additional troops and armored divisions are stationed to prevent insurgent
            activity from spilling over.
 3. Logistics Hubs:
            Supply depots are expanded to support long-term border operations.
