1987: Boombayah's Renaming and the Classified Coup
1. Brazil Officially Renamed "Boombayah"

Renaming Details:
Under Madison's leadership, Brazil adopts the new name "Boombayah," symbolizing its
energetic, unified, and modern identity. This name reflects its dominant position in South
America and signals its intent to lead with bold, unconventional policies.

Impacts of the Renaming:
 1. Cultural Rebranding:
            National symbols, including the flag and anthem, are updated to reflect the new
            identity.
            "Boombayah" is marketed as a forward-thinking, progressive nation.
 2. International Reactions:
            Many global leaders are puzzled by the sudden change, while allies rally behind
            Boombayah's boldness.
            Critics mock the rebranding as a distraction from internal challenges, including
            insurgencies in former Argentina.

2. Coup Staged by Unidentified Forces

Unidentified Coup Operation
An unidentified force initiates a covert operation to destabilize Boombayah by funding
and arming the nation's anarchist party, aiming to create widespread unrest and challenge
Madison's leadership.

Objectives:
 1. Political Destabilization:
            Overthrow Madison's government and install an anarchist regime.
 2. Undermine Regional Dominance:
            Prevent Boombayah from consolidating its hold over former Argentina and other
            South American territories.
Operation Plan:
Phase 1: Recruitment and Funding

      Objective: Strengthen the anarchist party's influence among Boombayah's working
      class and rural communities.
      Tactics:

            Covertly funnel funds and weapons to anarchist leaders.
            Distribute propaganda criticizing Madison's policies and highlighting corruption
            within the government.

Phase 2: Coordinated Protests and Strikes
      Objective: Paralyze Boombayah's infrastructure and economy.
      Tactics:
            Organize nationwide strikes in key industries, including agriculture and energy.
            Stage mass protests in major cities like Rio de Janeiro and Săo Paulo.

Phase 3: Military Coup
      Objective: Seize control of government institutions.
      Tactics:
            Infiltrate Boombayah's military and coordinate with sympathizers within the
            armed forces.
            Launch a coup targeting the presidential palace and key administrative buildings.

Outcome:
 1. Initial Success:
            Widespread protests and strikes disrupt Boombayah's economy, weakening
            Madison's hold on the nation.
            Armed anarchist groups seize control of several rural provinces, creating chaos.
 2. Government Retaliation:
            Madison declares martial law, deploying the military to suppress uprisings.
            Loyalist forces regain control of key cities, though unrest persists in rural areas.
 3. Classified Status of Unidentified Forces:
            The involvement of external forces remains undisclosed, though rumors of
            outside funding fuel distrust among Boombayah's populace.
3. Global Reactions

Boombayah:
      Internal Chaos:
            Madison's government faces its greatest challenge yet, with anarchist uprisings
            threatening to fracture the nation.
            Martial law and crackdowns on dissent strain public trust in the administration.

United Nations:
      Calls for Stability:
            The U.N. urges all parties in Boombayah to seek peaceful resolution, though no
            concrete actions are taken.

Neighboring Nations:
      Regional Instability:
            South American countries express concern over the potential spread of anarchist
            movements, strengthening their own defenses.

      among international observers.

      Madison's government fights to maintain control amid widespread unrest, with the

1. The L.E.T.F.'s Invasion of India

Operation Mystic Fade
The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) begins a massive invasion campaign
targeting India, aiming to annex the subcontinent and expand Morganism into South Asia.

Strategic Objectives:
 1. Territorial Expansion:
            Subjugate India and integrate it as a key province within the L.E.T.F. empire.
 2. Resource Access:
            Gain control of India's vast population, agricultural output, and industrial
            capacity.
 3. Religious Transformation:
            Replace traditional Indian religions with Morganism, solidifying ideological
            control.

Military Strategy:
Forces Deployed:

      Ground Troops:
            3.5 million soldiers, including mechanized infantry, artillery, and elite urban
            combat units.
            Fade Tanks and BMP-1s for frontline engagements.
      Air Force:
            MiG-21s, Su-17 bombers, and ceremonial propaganda jets broadcasting
            Morganist hymns.

      Naval Forces:
            Carrier strike groups blockade Indian ports like Mumbai and Chennai.
            Amphibious assault units target coastal regions for rapid landings.

Invasion Strategy:
 1. Northern Push:
            Forces advance through Himalayan passes, targeting Delhi and key northern
            cities.
            Airstrikes neutralize Indian military installations along the border.
 2. Southern Landings:
            Amphibious units secure coastal cities, including Mumbai and Chennai, cutting
            off supply routes.
 3. Central Campaign:
            Mechanized forces push into India's interior, aiming to capture industrial hubs
            and administrative centers.

Outcome:
 1. Partial Success:
            Northern India falls quickly, with Delhi and other key cities under L.E.T.F. control.
            Southern and central regions resist fiercely, with Indian forces rallying support.
 2. Insurgencies Form:
            Guerrilla resistance begins in rural and mountainous areas, supported by external
            funding.

the L.E.T.F. invasion and weaken its influence.

            supplies and logistics.
 2. Arms Shipments:
            Modernized tanks, aircraft, and naval vessels are delivered to Indian forces.
 3. Strategic Advisors:
            Boombayah sends military advisors to assist Indian commanders with strategy
            and coordination.

Outcome:
 1. Indian Counteroffensive:
            With Boombayah's support, Indian forces launch counterattacks in the south and
            east, slowing L.E.T.F. advances.
 2. Global Attention:
            Boombayah's involvement sparks international support for India, further isolating
            the L.E.T.F.

1987: L.E.T.F. Launches Full-Scale Invasion of Australia and Expands Campaign
in Boombayah

1. L.E.T.F. Full-Scale Invasion of Australia

Operation Emerald Fade
The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) begins its long-anticipated invasion of Australia,
aiming to secure control over the continent and establish dominance in the Pacific region.

Strategic Objectives:
 1. Territorial Control:
            Annex Australia as a key province within the L.E.T.F. empire.

 2. Resource Exploitation:
            Gain access to Australia's vast mineral wealth, agriculture, and strategic Pacific
            positioning.

Forces Deployed:
      Ground Troops:
            3 million soldiers, including amphibious assault units, mechanized infantry, and
            special forces trained for desert and urban combat.
            Fade Tanks and mobile artillery divisions.
      Air Force:
            MiG-21s, Su-17 bombers, and newly developed Fade Interceptors dominate the
            skies.
            Propaganda planes equipped with loudspeakers broadcast Morganist hymns over
            battle zones.
      Naval Forces:
            Carrier strike groups deploy along the northern and eastern coasts, targeting
            Darwin, Brisbane, and Sydney.
            Submarines blockade major ports to prevent foreign reinforcements.

Invasion Strategy:
Phase 1: Northern Landings

      Target: Darwin and Northern Territory
      Plan:

            Amphibious assault units secure Darwin, establishing a foothold for inland
            operations.
            Mechanized forces push southward, capturing key transportation hubs.
      Outcome:
            Darwin falls quickly, and northern Australia is under L.E.T.F. control.

Phase 2: Eastern Push
      Target: Brisbane and Sydney
      Plan:
            Naval bombardments and airstrikes soften defenses.
            Urban combat units storm Brisbane and Sydney, aiming to cripple Australian
            resistance.

      Outcome:
            Brisbane is captured, but Sydney sees intense resistance, delaying progress.

Phase 3: Central Domination
      Target: Outback and mining regions
      Plan:
            Mechanized divisions and air cavalry secure resource-rich areas to fuel the L.E.T.F.
            war machine.
      Outcome:
            Central Australia is contested, with guerrilla resistance from local forces.

Outcome:
 1. Partial Success:
            The L.E.T.F. controls northern and eastern Australia, but southern and central
            regions remain contested.
 2. Global Outcry:
            The invasion sparks outrage, with NATO and Pacific allies considering
            intervention.

1987: L.E.T.F. Martial Law in South America and Espionage Operations

1. L.E.T.F. Declares Martial Law in South American Territories

Operation Silent Suppression
The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) implements martial law across occupied South
American territories, aiming to crush resistance and solidify its annexation
of Boombayah and surrounding areas.

Objectives:
 1. Suppress Resistance:
            Eliminate guerrilla movements, anarchist factions, and remnants of Madison's
            forces.
 2. Stabilize Territories:
            Enforce Morganist rule and integrate annexed regions into the L.E.T.F. empire.

Measures Taken:
 1. Mass Deployments:
            An additional 500,000 troops are deployed to urban and rural areas, focusing on
            hotspots like the Amazon and Rio de Janeiro.

 2. Checkpoints and Curfews:
            Military checkpoints are established in major cities and along key transportation
            routes.
            Strict curfews are enforced, with violators detained or executed.

 3. Psychological Warfare:
            Morganist priests conduct public ceremonies, promoting loyalty to the L.E.T.F.
            Propaganda campaigns frame resistance as a threat to stability and progress.

Outcome:
 1. Resistance Weakened:
            Martial law disrupts guerrilla operations, though small-scale attacks persist in
            remote areas.
 2. Civilian Unrest:
            The heavy-handed approach sparks fear and resentment among civilians, risking
            long-term instability.

2. L.E.T.F. Espionage Operations and Hit List Development

Project Phantom Sky Collaboration
The L.E.T.F. collaborates with the United States to utilize the SR-91 Poltergeist, a cutting-
edge hypersonic reconnaissance aircraft developed under Project Phantom Sky, to
identify nations leading the global backlash against L.E.T.F. expansion.

Operation Watchful Fade
Objectives:

 1. Identify Hostile Nations:
            Use advanced reconnaissance to track countries opposing L.E.T.F. actions.

 2. Target Key Figures:
            Develop a hit list of political and military leaders orchestrating opposition to the
            L.E.T.F.

Reconnaissance Strategy:
Phase 1: Intelligence Gathering

      SR-91 Poltergeist Missions:
            The U.S.-aided reconnaissance aircraft flies undetected over target nations,
            gathering high-resolution imagery and signals intelligence.

      Spies and Operatives:
            L.E.T.F. agents infiltrate diplomatic missions, international organizations, and key
            institutions.

Phase 2: Data Analysis
      AI-Assisted Processing:
            Intelligence from the SR-91 and field agents is analyzed to identify hostile
            nations, their leaders, and potential weaknesses.
      Political Mapping:
            Nations are categorized based on their level of hostility, with strategic and
            actionable targets prioritized.

Preliminary Hit List:
 1. Nations Actively Opposing L.E.T.F.:
            Brazil (Boombayah): Guerrilla resistance and funding for insurgents.
            India (Exiled Forces): Supporting anti-L.E.T.F. movements globally.
            Australia: Insurgencies and appeals for NATO intervention.
            United Kingdom: Strong U.N. opposition and covert funding of resistance forces.
            Japan: Vocal condemnation of L.E.T.F. actions and naval build-up in the Pacific.
 2. Potential Future Threats:
            Canada: Increasing alignment with anti-L.E.T.F. coalitions.
            France: Diplomatic support for resistance forces in occupied territories.

Outcome:
 1. Global Hit List Compiled:
            The L.E.T.F. finalizes a list of high-value targets, including nations and individual
            leaders, for future action.

 2. Tensions Escalate:
            The espionage operation deepens mistrust and accelerates anti-L.E.T.F. efforts
            globally.

3. Global Reactions

United States:
      Collaborative Stance:
            The U.S. continues to assist the L.E.T.F., justifying the espionage operations as
            part of a broader effort to stabilize global power dynamics.

United Nations:
      Condemnation:
            The U.N. passes another resolution condemning martial law in South America and
            the invasion of Australia, though enforcement remains limited.

Resistance Movements:
      South America:
            Guerrilla forces regroup in the Amazon, adapting to martial law measures.
      Australia:
            Insurgencies gain support from Japan, the U.K., and NATO allies, complicating
            L.E.T.F. control.

4. Summary

      Espionage operations using the SR-91 Poltergeist identify nations opposing the

 1. Total Annexation:

            resistance pockets.

            Target: Madison's forces in the Amazon Basin.
            Plan: Coordinated airstrikes and ground operations aim to eliminate Madison's

            Plan: Mechanized units advance from Ukraine, capturing major cities like Kosice.

The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) expands its European campaign by

      Liechtenstein:
            While largely subdued, underground networks form to resist L.E.T.F. rule.

      Austria is renamed the "Alpine Province of the Fade," and Liechtenstein is absorbed

            1 million soldiers, including mountain warfare specialists and mechanized units.

            Switzerland.

            Target: Bern and mountainous regions.

            Outcome: Bern falls, though resistance in the Alps delays further progress.

 3. Phase 3: Western Sweep
            Target: Geneva and Lausanne.
            Plan: Special forces secure Geneva, while mechanized units advance into western
            Switzerland.
            Outcome: Geneva is captured, marking the collapse of Swiss resistance.

Outcome:
 1. Switzerland Annexed:
            Switzerland is declared part of the "Alpine Province of the Fade."
 2. Financial Takeover:

1987: Operation Watchful Fade 2

Objective:
The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) launches Operation Watchful Fade 2 to conduct
an advanced intelligence-gathering campaign. The operation seeks to identify:

 1. Countries actively opposing the L.E.T.F. and contributing to global backlash.
 2. Countries fearful of the L.E.T.F. that may remain neutral or become potential allies

      under pressure.
1. Operation Strategy

Reconnaissance Assets:
      SR-91 Poltergeist:
            Advanced U.S.-aided hypersonic reconnaissance aircraft conducts high-altitude
            surveillance, collecting real-time intelligence.
      Espionage Network:
            L.E.T.F. spies infiltrate diplomatic, military, and economic institutions in target
            nations.
      Signals Intelligence (SIGINT):
            Interception of communications to analyze diplomatic chatter and military plans.

Phases of Operation:
Phase 1: Global Survey

      Target: Nations suspected of spearheading global opposition.
      Plan:

            Conduct aerial and cyber surveillance on high-priority nations to track political
            and military activities.

Phase 2: Psychological Assessment
      Target: Nations remaining neutral or showing hesitancy.
      Plan:
            Analyze intercepted communications to gauge fear levels, diplomatic stances,
            and susceptibility to intimidation.

Phase 3: Categorization
      Deliverable:
            A categorized report of hostile nations, neutral states, and nations showing fear
            or potential willingness to align with the L.E.T.F.

2. Findings

Hostile Nations (Leading the Backlash):
 1. United Kingdom:
            Vocal at the U.N. and covertly supporting resistance movements in Switzerland
            and South Korea.
 2. Japan:
            Increasing military buildup in the Pacific and funding guerrilla forces in South
            Korea.
 3. France:
            Open condemnation of L.E.T.F. actions and rumored logistical support to
            European resistance networks.
 4. Australia:
            Insurgencies continue to resist L.E.T.F. occupation, supported by NATO allies.
 5. Brazil (Boombayah remnants):
            Madison's government-in-exile is regrouping with international backing in the
            Amazon.

Neutral Nations (Passive Observers):
 1. India (Exiled Forces):
            Limited activity outside South Asia, focusing on internal refugee crises.
 2. Germany:
            Avoids direct confrontation but increases border defenses and NATO
            commitments.
 3. Canada:
            Remains passive but aligns diplomatically with NATO.

Fearful Nations (Potential Targets or Allies):
 1. Italy:
            Publicly neutral but internally fears L.E.T.F. expansion into southern Europe.
 2. Saudi Arabia:
            Displays nervousness over L.E.T.F.'s growing influence in Asia and its potential
            reach into the Middle East.
 3. South Africa:
            Quietly strengthens its military but avoids provoking the L.E.T.F. to maintain
            neutrality.

3. Outcome
Key Insights:
 1. Global Opposition Identified:
            The U.K., Japan, and France are spearheading diplomatic and military backlash,
            with Australia and Boombayah remnants actively resisting on the ground.
 2. Potential Targets for Intimidation:
            Fearful nations like Italy and Saudi Arabia may be coerced into alignment or
            neutrality through targeted diplomacy and propaganda.

Next Steps for L.E.T.F.:
 1. Strategic Focus:
            Prioritize actions against hostile nations while leveraging fear to neutralize or
            align weaker states.
 2. Propaganda Campaigns:
            Deploy psychological operations to sway fearful nations and reduce global
            opposition.
 3. Military Planning:
            Prepare for potential retaliation or intervention from NATO or regional powers.

4. Summary

      Hostile Nations Identified:
            The U.K., Japan, France, Australia, and Boombayah remnants lead the backlash.

      Neutral Nations Monitored:
            Germany, Canada, and India remain passive but could shift positions based on
            global dynamics.

      Fearful Nations Categorized:
            Italy, Saudi Arabia, and South Africa exhibit apprehension, presenting
            opportunities for leverage.

1987: L.E.T.F. Invasion of Italy, San Marino, and Vatican City

Operation Roman Fade
The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) initiates a large-scale invasion of Italy, including
its enclaves San Marino and Vatican City, aiming to establish dominance over Southern
Europe and capitalize on the region's cultural and strategic value.

1. Strategic Objectives

 1. Territorial Expansion:
            Annex Italy, San Marino, and Vatican City into the "Southern European Province
            of the Fade."

 2. Symbolic Domination:
            Capture Rome and Vatican City to demonstrate ideological and religious
            superiority, replacing historic influence with Morganism.

 3. Economic and Strategic Control:
            Gain access to Italy's industrial base, Mediterranean ports, and cultural landmarks
            to strengthen the L.E.T.F.'s global position.

2. Military Strategy

Forces Deployed:
      Ground Troops:
            1.5 million soldiers, including mechanized infantry, mountain warfare units, and
            urban combat specialists.
            Fade Tanks and mobile artillery lead the ground offensive.
      Air Force:
            MiG-21s, Su-17 bombers, and drones conduct airstrikes on military installations
            and strategic infrastructure.
      Naval Forces:
            Amphibious units launch assaults on key coastal cities, supported by naval
            bombardments.
      Special Forces:
            Operatives infiltrate Rome and Vatican City to neutralize leadership and seize
            control of key sites.

Invasion Plan:
 1. Phase 1: Northern Offensive
            Target: Milan and Venice.
            Plan: Mechanized units advance from Switzerland, capturing key economic hubs
            in northern Italy.
            Outcome: Milan and Venice fall swiftly due to limited resistance.
 2. Phase 2: Central Advance
            Target: Florence and Rome.
            Plan: Ground forces push southward, with airstrikes and special forces targeting
            Rome and Vatican City.
            Outcome: Florence is captured, but resistance intensifies near Rome.
 3. Phase 3: Southern Campaign
            Target: Naples and southern Italy.
            Plan: Amphibious units land near Naples, cutting off escape routes and securing
            Mediterranean ports.
            Outcome: Southern Italy falls, though guerrilla resistance emerges in rural areas.
 4. Phase 4: Enclave Neutralization
            San Marino:
                  Overwhelmed by a single mechanized division; surrenders with minimal
                  resistance.
            Vatican City:
                  Special forces infiltrate and seize Vatican City, replacing religious leadership
                  with Morganist priests.

3. Outcome

Italy Annexed:
      Italy is declared the "Southern European Province of the Fade."

San Marino Annexed:
      San Marino is integrated into the Southern European Province with little opposition.

Vatican City Annexed:
      The Vatican is declared a Morganist Religious Center, with priests repurposing iconic
      landmarks for Morganist ceremonies.

4. Resistance and Fallout

Guerrilla Movements:
      Italy:
            Resistance forms in southern Italy and the Alps, disrupting supply lines and
            challenging L.E.T.F. control.

Global Reactions:
      United Nations:
            Condemns the invasion, calling it a cultural and religious atrocity.
      NATO:
            Mobilizes forces along neighboring borders, preparing for potential conflict with
            the L.E.T.F.

Symbolic Repercussions:
      The capture of Vatican City shocks the world, intensifying anti-L.E.T.F. sentiment and
      fueling resistance movements globally.

5. Summary

      The L.E.T.F. annexes Italy, San Marino, and Vatican City, expanding its empire into
      Southern Europe.
      Resistance movements emerge, supported by NATO and global anti-L.E.T.F. coalitions.
      The annexation of Vatican City creates significant symbolic backlash, strengthening
      opposition to the L.E.T.F.'s global ambitions.
What's next for the L.E.T.F.? Will it focus on consolidating its new territories, or will it
prepare for further expansion despite rising global tensions?

      installations.

      Marseille and Lyon.

 3. Phase 3: Southern Sweep
            Target: Marseille, Lyon, and surrounding areas.

            Outcome: Southern France is captured, but resistance continues in rural areas.

Outcome:

campaign targeting Congo, Zaire (now DRC), Angola, and Namibia, seeking to expand its
influence into Central and Southern Africa.

            minerals.

 3. Regional Dominance:
            Establish L.E.T.F. dominance over Africa and position for further expansion.

            reconnaissance.

            Amphibious assault ships target Angola's and Namibia's coastal regions.

 1. Phase 1: Congo and Zaire Offensive
            Target: Kinshasa and key resource-rich areas in Congo and Zaire.

                  Mechanized units advance from staging areas in Sudan and Central African
                  territories.
                  Airstrikes neutralize resistance in Kinshasa and Lubumbashi.

                  Kinshasa falls quickly, and Zaire's government collapses after heavy
                  bombardments.

            Target: Luanda and surrounding oil-rich regions.
            Plan:

                  Mechanized forces advance inland to capture key infrastructure.
            Outcome:

 3. Phase 3: Namibia Campaign

                  Amphibious units land along Namibia's coast, while ground forces push
                  southward from Angola.
            Outcome:
                  Windhoek falls after minimal resistance, securing Namibia under L.E.T.F.
                  control.

 1. Congo, Zaire, Angola, and Namibia Annexed:
            The territories are consolidated into the "Southern African Province of the
            Fade."
 2. Resistance Movements:

            warfare.

United Nations:
      Severe Condemnation:
            The U.N. denounces the invasion, demanding immediate withdrawal and

NATO:
      Increased Vigilance:
            NATO shifts resources to Africa, covertly supporting resistance movements with

            Some African nations condemn the annexations, while others align with the
            L.E.T.F., seeking economic and military benefits.
4. Resistance and Fallout

      Angola and Zaire:

Operation Albion Fade
The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) initiates a bold campaign to invade and annex

 1. Neutralize Opposition:
            Annex the United Kingdom as the "British Isles Province of the Fade."

 2. Control Strategic Assets:

            3 million soldiers, including mechanized infantry, amphibious units, and urban

 1. Phase 1: Naval and Aerial Dominance

 2. Phase 2: Amphibious Landings

 4. Phase 4: Northern Push

            Outcome:

      United Kingdom:
            Covert NATO support fuels insurgencies in rural areas and urban centers.

1989: L.E.T.F. Launches Invasion of the Arctic, North Pole, and South Pole

Operation Polar Fade
The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) launches an unprecedented campaign to annex
the Arctic, the North Pole, and the South Pole, seeking complete global dominance and
control over untapped resources in these extreme regions.

1. Strategic Objectives

 1. Territorial Domination:
            Annex the Arctic and Antarctic regions as the "Polar Provinces of the Fade."

 2. Resource Control:
            Seize control of the Arctic's vast oil, gas, and mineral reserves and Antarctica's
            untapped natural resources.

 3. Global Symbolism:
            Assert L.E.T.F. supremacy by conquering the last unclaimed territories on Earth.
 4. Military Expansion:

            Establish strategic bases in the Arctic and Antarctic to monitor and counter NATO
            and U.N. forces.

2. Military Strategy

Forces Deployed:
      Ground Troops:
            500,000 soldiers, including Arctic warfare specialists and heavy equipment for
            extreme conditions.
      Air Force:
            MiG-21s, Su-17 bombers, and drones equipped for cold-weather operations.
      Naval Forces:
            Icebreakers and amphibious assault ships to navigate polar waters.
            Submarines to secure underwater routes.

Invasion Plan:
 1. Phase 1: Arctic Offensive
            Target: Arctic territories claimed by NATO nations (Canada, Norway, Denmark,
            Russia).
            Plan:
                  Icebreakers and submarines secure naval routes.
                  Amphibious forces land near strategic Arctic settlements, including Svalbard
                  and Greenland's northern regions.
                  Ground forces establish bases at key resource sites.
            Outcome:
                  Arctic regions are annexed, though NATO scrambles to counter the incursion.
 2. Phase 2: North Pole Annexation
            Target: North Pole's central ice cap.
            Plan:
                  Military engineers establish a permanent base at the geographic North Pole.
                  Surveillance equipment and missile systems are deployed for global
                  monitoring.
            Outcome:
                  The North Pole is declared the "Northern Crown of the Fade."
 3. Phase 3: Antarctic Campaign
            Target: Antarctic research stations and natural reserves.
            Plan:
                  Amphibious forces land on key coasts, including McMurdo Station and
                  Queen Maud Land.
                  Airstrikes target opposition research stations and supply lines.
            Outcome:
                  Antarctica is annexed, renamed the "Southern Crown of the Fade."

3. Outcome

Territories Annexed:
 1. Arctic Region:
            Includes areas previously controlled by NATO nations, Greenland, and Svalbard.
 2. North Pole:
            Declared the "Northern Crown of the Fade."
 3. Antarctica:
            Declared the "Southern Crown of the Fade."

Resistance Movements:
      Limited due to the sparsity of populations, but NATO begins reinforcing northern
      territories and funding resistance movements.

4. Global Reactions

United Nations:
      Worldwide Condemnation:
            The U.N. declares the annexations illegal, urging immediate withdrawal and
            imposing strict sanctions.
NATO:
      Retaliatory Planning:
            NATO mobilizes Arctic forces, deploying additional submarines and aircraft to
            counter L.E.T.F. control in the North.
Environmental Concerns:
      Global Activism:
            Environmental groups protest the exploitation of polar regions, demanding
            immediate international intervention.

5. Summary

      The L.E.T.F. successfully annexes the Arctic, North Pole, and South Pole, creating
      the Polar Provinces of the Fade.
      Global tensions escalate as NATO and the U.N. condemn the annexations and prepare
      for potential confrontation.
      Environmental and logistical challenges persist as the L.E.T.F. begins resource
      extraction and military fortification in these extreme regions.

sights to South America and Africa for further conquest?

The L.E.T.F. launched a major invasion of Jamaica, deploying a large number of troops,

bases to secure their control over the Caribbean region.

forming guerrilla movements to reclaim their homeland. The cultural and national spirit of
Jamaica remains strong, even under occupation.

1989: L.E.T.F. Invasion of South America

 3. Regional Power:

      Fade."

Operation Nordic Breakpoint
With West Germany and Denmark launching a catastrophic nuclear strike targeting

Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) retaliates by initiating its final annexation campaign to
conquer the last NATO strongholds: West Germany and Denmark. This operation sees
unprecedented military engagements, including the deployment of advanced aircraft and

 1. Complete NATO Collapse:
            Eliminate West Germany and Denmark as the last standing NATO members.

 3. Global Consolidation:

            Deter the L.E.T.F. with nuclear strikes on major capitals.

            counteroffensives.

L.E.T.F. Forces:
      Ground Troops:
            5.5 million soldiers, including mechanized infantry, urban combat specialists, and

            Fade Tanks deployed en masse to breach fortified defenses.

            Sukhoi Su-24s for deep-strike missions and strategic bombing.

            Advanced drones for reconnaissance and battlefield targeting.

            Amphibious assault units deployed to secure Danish coastal regions.

      Aircraft Deployed:
            A-12 Archangel and YF-12 prototypes launched for high-speed reconnaissance
            and interception.
            Advanced interceptors deployed to neutralize NATO air defenses and nuclear
            capabilities.

West Germany & Denmark Forces:
      Ground Troops:
            Combined force of 3 million soldiers, heavily concentrated in fortified urban
            centers and strategic choke points.

            for defensive operations.
      Nuclear Arsenal:
            Tactical and strategic nuclear weapons deployed against L.E.T.F. capitals and
            troop concentrations.

      Target: Copenhagen and surrounding regions.
      Plan:
            Amphibious forces land near Copenhagen, supported by naval bombardments

      Target: NATO air forces and nuclear launch sites.
      Plan:
            L.E.T.F. interceptors neutralize NATO aircraft, including high-speed engagements
            with the A-12 Archangel and YF-12 prototypes.
            Reconnaissance drones locate and destroy remaining nuclear silos.
      Outcome:
            NATO air superiority diminishes, though significant nuclear fallout disrupts L.E.T.F.
            operations.

4. Outcome

Territories Annexed:
 1. Denmark: Integrated as the "Nordic Province of the Fade."
 2. West Germany: Declared the "Western European Province of the Fade."

Global Impact:
      The collapse of NATO marks the end of organized Western resistance to the L.E.T.F.
      Major nuclear devastation affects global populations, particularly in previously
      targeted L.E.T.F. capitals.

Military Losses:
      L.E.T.F. forces suffer significant casualties and equipment losses due to nuclear strikes.
      West Germany and Denmark lose nearly all remaining military assets, effectively
      ending NATO as a military alliance.

5. Global Reactions

United Nations:
      Declaration of Collapse:
            The U.N. ceases operations due to the scale of global destruction and the
            dominance of the L.E.T.F.

United States:
      Alliance Strengthened:
            The U.S. continues its support of the L.E.T.F., consolidating power in the Americas
            while remaining an ally.

Remaining Nations:
      Resistance Movements:
            Insurgencies persist in former NATO territories, but their impact is minimal
            compared to L.E.T.F.'s global power.

6. Summary

      The L.E.T.F. successfully annexes Denmark and West Germany, completing the
      collapse of NATO and asserting dominance over Europe.
      Nuclear strikes devastate L.E.T.F. capitals, but its military infrastructure survives to
      maintain control.
      The global balance of power is irrevocably shifted, with the L.E.T.F. and its allies
      standing unchallenged on the world stage.

1989: L.E.T.F. Final Global Conquest

Operation Eternal Fade
The Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) embarks on its final conquest to achieve total
global domination, targeting all remaining unclaimed countries in Africa. Exhausting all its
military firepower and resources, the L.E.T.F. consolidates its empire in a campaign of
unparalleled scale. Simultaneously, it focuses on rebuilding and honoring its cultural and
political icons, cementing its legacy as a global power.

1. Strategic Overview

Reconstruction Goals:
 1. City Repairs:
            Rebuild major capitals such as Cairo, Fade's Crown (formerly Kaliningrad), and
            others devastated by nuclear strikes.
            Reestablish infrastructure and urban centers to stabilize the L.E.T.F.'s global
            territories.
 2. Cultural and Political Focus:
            Honor significant figures:
                  King Darius Morgan: Strengthened as the spiritual and political leader.
                  Adolf Hitler: Monitored as vice ruler under specialized medical care.
                  Magnus Maximus's Grave: Memorial expanded to honor his role in the
                  empire's foundation.
                  Gorg Morgan and Vex Bolts: Revered as deities in the L.E.T.F. pantheon.
                  Mr. Clean: Celebrated as the Goddess of Happiness and Lightning,
                  symbolizing purification and power.

Military Goals:
 1. Complete African Annexation:
            Invade and annex all unclaimed African nations, unifying the continent under
            L.E.T.F. control.
 2. Total Global Domination:
            Establish the L.E.T.F.-U.S. alliance as the only global powers, eliminating all other
            sovereign nations.

2. Military Strategy

Forces Deployed:
      Ground Troops:
            8 million soldiers, including mechanized infantry, urban combat specialists, and
            desert warfare units.
            Fade Tanks and heavy artillery used for sweeping operations.
      Air Force:
            Sukhoi Su-24s, MiG-21s, and advanced drones for air superiority and precision
            strikes.
      Naval Forces:
            Amphibious assault ships and submarines patrol coastal regions to support
            invasions of Madagascar and coastal nations.
Invasion Plan:
 1. Phase 1: East African Offensive
            Targets: Ethiopia, Somalia, Kenya, Tanzania, Zambia, Zimbabwe, Mozambique,
            and Madagascar.
            Plan:
                  Mechanized units advance through the Horn of Africa and Great Lakes
                  region, while amphibious forces land in Madagascar.
            Outcome:
                  East Africa is annexed after heavy fighting in urban and rural areas.
 2. Phase 2: West African Campaign
            Targets: Benin, Togo, Nigeria, Ghana, Ivory Coast, Sierra Leone, Liberia, and
            Burkina Faso.
            Plan:
                  Ground forces secure coastal and inland regions, targeting capitals and key
                  industrial centers.
            Outcome:
                  West Africa is annexed after prolonged combat in Nigeria and Ghana.
 3. Phase 3: Sahel and North African Sweep
            Targets: Mali, Mauritania, Senegal, Gambia, Guinea-Bissau, and Equatorial Guinea.
            Plan:
                  Airstrikes weaken resistance in desert regions, allowing mechanized forces to
                  secure strategic locations.
            Outcome:
                  The Sahel is annexed with minimal resistance; North Africa, including Egypt,
                  is fully under L.E.T.F. control.

3. Outcome

Territories Annexed:
      Entire African Continent: Unified under the "African Province of the Fade."

Resistance Movements:
      Minor Insurgencies:
            Resistance forms in remote regions, but the sheer scale of L.E.T.F. firepower
            suppresses most uprisings.

4. Global Reactions

United Nations:
      Dissolved:
            With no remaining member nations, the U.N. ceases to exist.

Global Landscape:
      The world is now divided between:
            L.E.T.F. Territories: Covering all of Africa, Europe, Asia, the Middle East, Australia,
            and parts of the Americas.
            United States: Maintaining control over the Americas outside of L.E.T.F. territories.

Cultural Legacy:
      King Darius Morgan and other revered figures become symbols of the new global
      order.
      Major capitals are rebuilt to reflect the L.E.T.F.'s dominance, blending modern
      architecture with monuments to its leaders.

5. Summary

      The L.E.T.F. successfully annexes the entire African continent, achieving global
      dominance alongside its ally, the United States.
      Resistance movements are minimal, with L.E.T.F. forces solidifying control over all
      annexed territories.
      The world is now fully divided between the L.E.T.F. and the United States, marking a
      new era of global power.

1989: L.E.T.F. vs. United States - The Final Global War

Operation Total Fade (LETF)

Operation Liberty Storm (United States)
With the Lowest Egyptian Taper Fade (L.E.T.F.) backstabbing its former ally, the United
States of America, and declaring war, the final global conflict erupts. Both sides deploy full
nuclear arsenals and commit their entire populations to the battlefield. This
unprecedented war results in catastrophic casualties and global devastation, marking the
potential end of civilization as it is known.

1. Strategic Objectives
L.E.T.F. Goals:
 1. Eliminate U.S. Leadership:
            Target the White House, NORAD, and key U.S. military installations with nuclear
            strikes.
            Neutralize American military power through total war.
 2. Protect Leadership:
            Defend King Darius Morgan, Adolf Hitler, Mr. Clean, and other leaders at all
            costs.
 3. Conquer the U.S. Homeland:
            Deploy half the army to invade and occupy American territories.

United States Goals:
 1. Destroy L.E.T.F. Leadership:
            Launch nuclear strikes targeting L.E.T.F. capitals and leaders' residences,
            including Cairo, Fade's Crown, and L.E.T.F.-controlled Washington, D.C.
 2. Establish Air Superiority:
            Deploy the full U.S. Air Force, including F-22 Raptors, B-2 Bombers, and SR-71
            reconnaissance aircraft to dominate L.E.T.F. airspace.
 3. Strengthen Defense:
            Heighten NORAD awareness, deploy radar systems, and fortify all U.S. territories
            and key locations.

2. Military Engagement

Nuclear Arsenal Deployment:
      L.E.T.F.:
            Launches nuclear missiles targeting Washington, D.C., the Pentagon, NORAD, and
            major U.S. cities.
            Uses tactical nukes on U.S. military bases and troop concentrations.
      United States:
            Launches ICBMs targeting Cairo, Fade's Crown, occupied European capitals, and
            L.E.T.F. leadership residences.
            Targets monuments to King Darius Morgan, Magnus Maximus, and others.

Ground Invasion:
      L.E.T.F. Invasion of the United States:
            Half the L.E.T.F. military, 10 million soldiers, invades the U.S. via amphibious
            assaults on the East Coast and Mexico.
            Intense fighting breaks out in major U.S. cities and along the borders.
      U.S. Counterattacks:
            U.S. forces deploy across the American heartland, defending key cities and
            launching counteroffensives into L.E.T.F.-controlled territories.
            Air superiority cripples L.E.T.F. troop movements.

Air and Naval Combat:
      L.E.T.F. Air Force:
            Deploys MiG-21s, Su-24s, and F-16s for bombing runs and dogfights.
      U.S. Air Force:
            Gains air superiority with F-22 Raptors, B-2 Bombers, and experimental aircraft
            like the YF-12.
      Naval Engagements:
            The U.S. Navy intercepts L.E.T.F. amphibious forces with carrier strike groups,
            submarines, and missile destroyers.

3. Outcome

Global Devastation:
      Casualties:
            Hundreds of millions die from nuclear strikes, conventional warfare, and resulting
            famine and disease.
            The world's population is decimated, with civilian and military losses on both
            sides.
      Infrastructure:
            Major cities on both sides are annihilated, leaving vast areas uninhabitable due to
            radiation and destruction.
      L.E.T.F. Leadership:
            King Darius Morgan and Adolf Hitler survive initial strikes in fortified bunkers
            but are ultimately captured or killed by U.S. special forces.
            Mr. Clean and Vex Bolts are presumed dead in nuclear blasts.
      United States Leadership:
            The White House is destroyed, but NORAD remains operational, coordinating
            surviving U.S. forces.

Military Outcome:
      L.E.T.F. Defeat:
            Exhausting its resources and manpower, the L.E.T.F. is unable to sustain its global
            conquest.
            Remaining territories collapse into chaos, with resistance movements reclaiming
            regions.
      U.S. Survival:
            Despite massive losses, the United States retains military superiority and begins
            rebuilding.

4. Global Aftermath

      World Population:
            Reduced by over 70%, with entire cities and regions rendered uninhabitable.

      Political Collapse:
            The L.E.T.F. is disbanded, its territories fragmented into ungoverned regions.

      U.S. Reconstruction:
            The United States emerges as the only organized superpower, focusing on
            rebuilding its homeland and stabilizing former L.E.T.F. territories.

5. Summary
      The final war between the L.E.T.F. and the United States results in the annihilation of
      both empires' infrastructures, but the U.S. survives as the dominant global power.
      The L.E.T.F. is destroyed, its leaders eliminated, and its territories fragmented.
      The world enters a new dark age, with survivors struggling to rebuild in a post-
      apocalyptic landscape.

conflict?
